Salah — Prayer

The Sunnah of the Sitting Between Prostrations and Du'a Therein
Analysis of the ruling on sitting between sajdatayn and the du'a there.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsa) as sunnah, explain why the school holds it as sunnah despite the Prophet's continuous practice, and identify the correct du'a for this position in fard prayer.

Core Idea
The jalsa between sajdatayn is sunnah, not wajib, and no specific du'a is recommended in fard prayer.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies two important points in the Hanafi school regarding the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsa). First, the ruling itself: is it sunnah or wajib? Second, what du'a should be recited at this juncture? The author addresses a common misconception that the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) makes it obligatory, and explains the Hanafi position that it is sunnah. He also derives from the school that no specific supplication is prescribed in the fard prayer for this sitting, interpreting any transmitted du'a as applying to supererogatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm
The passage discusses the sitting between the two prostrations (al-julus bayna al-sajdatayn). Determine its ruling: Is it wajib or sunnah?
The author states that the matn indicates the action is performed, then comments on its ruling.
2
Analyze the proof: Muwazabah
The author notes that the implication of the evidence from continuous practice (muwazabah) is obligation, but the Hanafi school is contrary. Understand the Hanafi usul principle: muwazabah alone does not make something wajib without a definitive command (amr).
This is a key usul principle distinguishing Hanafi from other schools.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Some later scholars (e.g., in Sharh al-Munya) argued for wujub from the perspective of diraya (rational understanding). The author distinguishes between diraya and riwaya (transmitted reports).
The author concedes the strength of diraya but maintains the school's position based on riwaya.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The majority of Hanafi commentators (sharihun) affirm sunniyyah. The relied-upon position is that the sitting is sunnah.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Address the du'a issue
The matn author did not mention a recommended dhikr. The Hanafi school holds that no specific du'a is said in fard prayer at this point; any reported du'a applies to tahajjud (supererogatory prayer).
The anecdote from Ya'qub confirms that Abu Hanifa only prescribed 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' after ruku', and similarly for the sitting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ثم رفع رأسه مكبراً وجلس مطمئناً) يعني بين السجدتين، وقد تقدم أن هذا الجلوس مسنون ومقتضى الدليل من المواظبة عليها وجوبها لكن المذهب خلافه، وما في شرح المنية من أن الأصح وجوبها إن كان بالنظر إلى الدراية فمسلم لما علمت من المواظبة، وإن كان من جهة الرواية فلا، وقد صرح الشارحون بالسنية. ولم يذكر المصنف بين السجدتين ذكراً مسنوناً وهو المذهب عندنا، وكذا بعد الرفع من الركوع، وما ورد فيهما من الدعاء فمحمول على التهجد قال يعقوب : سألت أبا حنيفة عن الرجل يرفع رأسه من الركوع في الفريضة أيقول اللهم اغفر لي قال : يقول ربنا لك الحمد وسكت. وكذلك بين السجدتين فقد أحسن حيث لم ينهه عن الاستغفار صريحاً من قوّة احترازه، ولم يذكر المصنف من هذا
His statement (then he raises his head saying takbir and sits with tranquility) means between the two prostrations. And it has preceded that this sitting is sunnah, and the implication of the evidence from continuous practice is its obligation, but the school is contrary to that. And what is in Sharh al-Munya that the correct view is its obligation if considered from the perspective of understanding (diraya) is conceded, because you have known the continuous practice; but if from the perspective of narration (riwaya), then no. And the commentators have stated its being sunnah. The author did not mention a recommended dhikr between the two prostrations, and that is the school in our view, and similarly after rising from ruku'. And what has been reported of du'a in both positions is interpreted as for tahajjud (supererogatory prayer). Ya'qub said: I asked Abu Hanifa about a man who raises his head from ruku' in the obligatory prayer, should he say 'Allahumma ighfir li'? He said: He says 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' and remained silent. And similarly between the two prostrations. So he (the author) did well in not explicitly prohibiting him from seeking forgiveness, due to the strength of his caution, and the author did not mention from this...
Source pages p. 561

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the sitting between the two prostrations (jalsa) and the du'a that may be said there. The author comments on the matn: 'then he raises his head saying takbir and sits with tranquility'. He explains that the sitting between sajdatayn is sunnah, not wajib. The apparent implication of the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah) might suggest obligation, but the Hanafi school holds it as sunnah. The author notes that some later scholars (e.g. in Sharh al-Munya) have said the correct view is that it is obligatory when considered from the perspective of rational understanding (diraya), since the Prophet did it always, but from the perspective of transmitted reports (riwaya) it is not. However, the relied-upon position is sunnah. Then the author states that the matn author did not mention a prescribed dhikr for this sitting, and that is the Hanafi school: no specific du'a is recommended in the fard prayer for the sitting between sajdatayn or after rising from ruku'. Any du'a reported for these positions is interpreted as for tahajjud (nafl). He cites the incident of Ya'qub asking Abu Hanifa: for the raising from ruku', only 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' is said; no other du'a (like seeking forgiveness) is prescribed. He commends the matn author for not explicitly forbidding such du'a, because it might be an act of caution. The passage clarifies that the jalsa is sunnah and no specific dhikr is mandub, but saying du'a is not disliked.

Key Terms
الجلوس بين السجدتين (al-julus bayna al-sajdatayn): The sitting posture after the first prostration before the second prostration, with tranquility.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): The Prophet's continuous practice; in Hanafi usul, constant practice without command indicates sunnah, not wajib.
التهجد (al-tahajjud): Supererogatory night prayer; here used to indicate that any du'a reported for the sitting is for nafl prayer, not fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does Ya'qub report from Abu Hanifa about saying 'Allahumma ighfir li' after rising from ruku' in fard prayer?
A) It is recommended
B) It is disliked
C) He said nothing, indicating it is not said
D) He said to say it

Key Takeaway
The sitting between sajdatayn is sunnah, and no specific du'a is prescribed in fard prayer at that point.

Standing Up from Sujud: The Hanafi Position on Using Hands
Hanafi-Shafi'i dispute on standing up from sujud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using hands when standing up from sujud, explain the evidence from hadith, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Standing up from sujud without hands is sunnah; using hands is makruh tanzihan — the dispute is about preference, not validity.

When you stand up after sujud in an odd rak'ah, should you push up with your hands? The Hanafi school teaches that it is best to stand without using hands, relying on the thighs and knees. Yet, the Shafi'i school sees it as permissible. This lesson unpacks the evidence and clarifies that the difference is one of preference, not of invalidating the prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: standing without hands is sunnah; using hands is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful).
This is the mufta bihi position, as the author prefers.
2
Identify the Hanafi proof
Find the hadith cited: Abu Dawud forbidding using hands; Wa'il describing the Prophet standing on knees and thighs; Abu Hurayra about standing on tops of feet.
These are dalil naqli (textual evidence).
3
Present the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet sat up straight before standing, and the general command 'Pray as you have seen me praying'.
This hadith appears in Bukhari.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi interpretation is that the sitting was due to the Prophet's old age; the command about praying as seen is general and does not specify every detail. The disagreement is about afdaliyya (preference), not validity.
Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani confirms the difference is only on what is better.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi considers using hands disliked but prayer valid; Shafi'i considers it permissible. Both agree the prayer is valid.
The Hanafi mufta bihi is to avoid hands, but if done, it is acceptable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وكبر للنهوض بلا اعتماد وقعود الحديث أبي داود : نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الرجل على يديه إذا نهض في الصلاة وفي حديث وائل بن حجر في صفة صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : وإذا نهض نهض على ركبتيه واعتمد على فخذيه والحديث الترمذي عن أبي هريرة أن النبي كان ينهض في الصلاة على صدور قدميه. قال الترمذي : إن عليه العمل عند أهل العلم. وأما ما رواه البخاري عن مالك بن الحويرث أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان في وتر من صلاته لم ينهض حتى يستوي قاعداً فمحمول على حالة الكبر كما في الهداية، ويرد عليه أن هذا الحمل يحتاج إلى دليل وقد قال عليه الصلاة والسلام لمالك بن الحويرث لما أراد أن يفارقه : صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي. ولم يفصل فكان الحديث حجة للشافعي، فالأولى أن يحمل على تعليم الجواز فلذا والله أعلم قال في الفتاوى الظهيرية قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : إن الخلاف إنما هو في الأفضلية حتى لو فعل كما هو مذهب الشافعي لا بأس به عندنا اهـ. وكذا ترك الاعتماد مستحب لمن ليس به عذر عندنا على ما هو ظاهر كثير من الكتب المشهورة. قال الوبري : لا بأس بأن يعتمد براحتيه على الأرض عند النهوض من غير فصل بين العذر وعدمه. ومثله ما في المحيط عن الطحاوي: لا بأس بأن يعتمد بيديه على الأرض شيخاً كان أو شاباً. وهو قول عامة العلماء اهـ. والأوجه أن يكون سنة فتركه يكره تنزيهاً لما تقدم من النهي . وذكر الشارح أنه يكره تقديم إحدى الرجلين عند النهوض، ويستحب مراعاة الخلاف وهذا منه كما لا يخفى. نعم لو كان الدعاء المذكور منهياً عنه عندنا لا تستحب المراعاة لما يلزم عليها من الخروج عن المذهب لكن ثبوت الكراهة يحتاج إلى دليل
His statement (and he says takbir for standing up without relying and sitting). The hadith of Abu Dawud: The Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade the man from (using) his hands when standing up in prayer. And in the hadith of Wa'il ibn Hujr describing the prayer of the Messenger of God: When he stood up, he stood on his knees and relied on his thighs. And the hadith of al-Tirmidhi from Abu Hurayra that the Prophet used to stand up in prayer on the tops of his feet. Al-Tirmidhi said: The practice is upon it according to the people of knowledge. As for what al-Bukhari narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that he saw the Prophet, when he was in an odd rak'ah of his prayer, he did not stand up until he sat up straight, it is interpreted as due to old age as in al-Hidayah. It is objected that this interpretation requires evidence, and the Prophet said to Malik ibn al-Huwayrith when he was about to leave: Pray as you have seen me praying, and he did not distinguish, so the hadith is evidence for al-Shafi'i. Therefore, it is better to interpret it as teaching permissibility. For this reason, God knows best, it is said in al-Fatawa al-Zahiriyya, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The disagreement is only about what is better (afdaliyya); so if one acts according to the Shafi'i school, it is acceptable with us. End. Similarly, leaving reliance is recommended (mustahabb) for one who has no excuse according to us, as is apparent in many famous books. Al-Wabiri said: There is no harm in relying with his palms on the ground when standing up, without distinction between excuse and no excuse. Similarly, what is in al-Muhit from al-Tahawi: There is no harm in relying with his hands on the ground, whether old or young. And it is the statement of the majority of scholars. End. And the most appropriate view is that it is sunnah, and leaving it is disliked (makruh tanzihan) due to the prohibition that preceded. And the commentator mentioned that it is disliked to put forward one foot when standing up, and it is recommended to consider the disagreement (mur'at al-khilaf), and this is from him as is not hidden. Yes, if the mentioned du'a were prohibited with us, then consideration of the disagreement would not be recommended because it would entail leaving the school, but establishing dislike requires evidence.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the manner of standing up from sujud (the 'third' rak'ah) in prayer. The matn states: 'and he says takbir for standing up without relying and sitting'. The commentator explains that according to a hadith in Abu Dawud, the Prophet forbade a man from using his hands to push up when standing. Another hadith from Wa'il ibn Hujr describes the Prophet standing on his knees and leaning on his thighs. A third hadith from Abu Hurayra (in Tirmidhi) says the Prophet stood on the tops of his feet (without hands). Tirmidhi considered this the practice of the scholars. However, a hadith from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith (in Bukhari) reports that the Prophet sat up straight before standing in odd rak'ahs. This is interpreted by Hanafis as due to old age, as in al-Hidayah. But this interpretation is contested by the Shafi'i school, who argue that the Prophet's command 'Pray as you have seen me praying' makes the general practice binding. The Hanafi response, from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, is that the disagreement is only about which is better (afdaliyya), not about validity. Therefore, using hands is permissible but not recommended. According to many Hanafi books, standing without reliance (i.e., using hands) is recommended (mustahabb). Al-Wabiri and al-Tahawi hold that relying is permissible without restriction. The author concludes that the most appropriate view is that standing without reliance is sunnah, and relying (especially using hands on ground) is makruh tanzihan. He also notes that it is disliked to put one foot forward when standing, and recommends 'mur'at al-khilaf' (taking into account the difference of opinion) by not doing what is disliked in other schools, provided it does not violate Hanafi ruling.

Key Terms
النهوض (al-nuhud): Standing up from sujud to the next rak'ah, especially in odd rak'ats (e.g., from sajda to third rak'ah).
الاعتماد (al-i'timad): Relying on hands (or knees) when standing up from sujud.
مراعاة الخلاف (mur'at al-khilaf): Taking into account the conflicting opinion of another school to avoid anything that might be considered disliked or invalid by them, as long as it does not violate one's own school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling on a healthy young person relying on his hands when standing up from sujud?
A) It is haram and invalidates prayer.
B) It is makruh tanzihan (disliked but not sinful).
C) It is mustahabb (recommended).
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that standing from sujud without hands is sunnah; using hands is makruh tanzihan, and the dispute with the Shafi'is is about preference, not validity.

The Minimum Lifting Between Prostrations: Four Narrations and Their Reconciliation
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the minimum valid lifting between prostrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four narrations from Abu Hanifa on the minimum valid lifting between prostrations, explain the differences, and identify the preferred (mufta bihi) position.

Core Idea
The jalsa between prostrations is valid with the minimum customarily called 'raising' — the preferred view from four narrations.

The sitting between the two prostrations (jalsa) is a required element of prayer. But how much lifting from prostration is needed? This lesson examines four narrations from Abu Hanifa that define the minimum, showing how later Hanafi scholars resolved the internal dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The passage addresses the minimum amount of lifting (raf') that separates the two prostrations, which determines whether the jalsa is valid.
2
List the four narrations
Four views from Abu Hanifa: (1) closer to sitting than prostration (al-Hidayah), (2) no doubt for the observer (al-Bada'i), (3) minimum to which the name 'raising' applies (al-Muhit), (4) enough for wind to pass (weak, unauthenticated).
3
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
Sahib al-Muhit's view (third) is preferred because it is qiyas to other pillars, where the obligatory minimum is the minimum that the name applies to.
Al-Ramli suggests the first two narrations may collapse into one: if closer to sitting, observer doubt vanishes.
4
State the mufta bihi
The operative position is the third narration: the minimum that is conventionally called 'raising' suffices. This is endorsed by the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أيضاً مقدار الرفع الذي يكون فاصلاً بين السجدتين للاختلاف فيه، فإن فيه أربع روايات عن أبي حنيفة صحح صاحب الهداية أنه إن كان إلى القعود أقرب جاز، وإن كان إلى السجود أقرب لا يجوز لأنه يعد ساجداً. وصحح صاحب البدائع أنه إن كان بحيث لا يشكل على الناظر أنه رفع يجوز . وصحح صاحب المحيط أنه يكتفي بأدنى ما ينطلق عليه اسم الرفع. والرواية الرابعة أنه إذا رفع رأسه مقدار ما يمر الريح بينه وبين الأرض جاز، ولم أر من صححها. وظاهر كلام المصنف في الكافي أنها تعود إلى الرواية الثالثة المصححة في المحيط واختارها فيه، وذكر أنها القياس لتعلق الركنية بالأدنى في سائر الأركان. قوله: (وصحح صاحب البدائع) قال الرملي : لقائل أن يقول : إن الرواية الثانية تعود إلى الرواية الأولى إذ بكونه إلى القعود أقرب يزول الإشكال على الناظر أنه رفع فيكون في المسألة روايتان فقط، وقد اقتصر منلامسكين على نقل الأولى والرابعة فقط ففيه إيماء لما قلنا فقط تأمل اهـ . وفي النهر : ولا يخفى قرب الثاني من الأول.
Also, the measure of lifting that is a separator between the two prostrations because of the difference of opinion: there are four narrations from Abu Hanifa. The author of al-Hidayah authenticated that if it is closer to sitting, it is permissible; if it is closer to prostration, it is not permissible because he is considered prostrating. The author of al-Bada'i authenticated that if it is such that a viewer would have no doubt that he is raising, it is permissible. The author of al-Muhit authenticated that one is satisfied with the minimum to which the name 'raising' applies. The fourth narration is that if he raises his head the amount for wind to pass between him and the ground, it is permissible; I have not seen anyone authenticate it. The apparent statement of the author in al-Kafi is that it returns to the third narration authenticated in al-Muhit, and he chose it there, and he mentioned that it is the qiyas because the obligatory nature (rukniyya) is attached to the minimum in all other pillars. His statement: (And authenticated by the author of al-Bada'i) al-Ramli said: One could say that the second narration returns to the first, for if it is closer to sitting, the doubt on the part of the viewer that it is raising is removed; thus there are only two narrations in this issue. And they relied on [؟] only for the first and fourth, and in that there is an indication of what we said. Consider. And in al-Nahr: the closeness of the second to the first is not hidden.
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the precise legal definition of 'raising' (raf') between the two prostrations, known as jalsa (sitting) in prayer. The author is explaining a dispute within the Hanafi school, specifically four narrations from Abu Hanifa regarding the minimum valid amount of lifting of the head from prostration to the sitting position. The first narration, preferred by al-Hidayah, sets the boundary: if the person is closer to sitting than to prostration, it is valid. The second narration, from al-Bada'i, uses an objective observer criterion: if a viewer would have no doubt that the person is raising, it is valid. The third narration, from al-Muhit, adopts the most lenient view: any movement that is linguistically called 'raising' suffices. The fourth narration (barely raising enough for air to pass) is rejected as unauthenticated. The author of al-Kafi sides with the third view, reasoning by qiyas that just as in other prayer pillars (ruku, sujood) the minimum suffices, so too in jalsa. Later, al-Ramli comments that the first and second narrations may actually reduce to one: if the raising is closer to sitting, observer doubt vanishes. The overall preferred view is the third, as it aligns with the principle of taking the minimum for rukniyya.

Key Terms
الرفع (al-raf'): The lifting of the head from prostration between the two prostrations; the minimum amount needed for a valid jalsa
الجلسة (al-jalsah): The sitting between the two prostrations

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which narration is preferred by the author of al-Muhit and supported by qiyas?
A) Closer to sitting than prostration
B) No doubt for the observer
C) Minimum to which the name 'raising' applies
D) Amount for wind to pass

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the minimum that is conventionally called 'raising' for the jalsa between prostrations, following the third narration and qiyas.

The Ruling on Rising in Prayer: Reliance on Hands
Examination of the Hanafi position on rising without relying on hands, with evidence from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on rising without relying on hands and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using dalil naqli.

Core Idea
Rising in prayer without hand support is sunnah; relying on hands is valid but disliked tanzihi.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq examines the recommended method of rising from prostration to standing. The Hanafi school, based on multiple hadiths, holds that one should rise without using hands for support. However, the Shafi'i school sees reliance as permissible. The text reconciles these views through the concept of khilaf al-awla (difference in preference).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is rising (al-nuhud) in prayer. The Hanafi ruling: it is sunnah (mustahab) to rise without hands; reliance is makruh tanzihi.
2
Locate the Hanafi dalil
The passage cites hadith from Abu Dawood (prohibition of hands), Wail ibn Hajar (rising on knees and thighs), and Tirmidhi (rising on soles of feet).
These are ahad hadith, giving zanni dalala.
3
Analyse the Shafi'i objection
The Shafi'i school uses the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet did not rise until fully seated, and the general command 'Pray as you have seen me pray.'
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response interprets the Malik hadith as a case of old age or teaching permission. Al-Halwani states the difference is only in preference (afdaliyya).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The difference is in preferability; a Hanafi who relies on hands is still valid but leaves the preferred practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وكبر للنهوض بلا اعتماد وقعود الحديث أبي داود : نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن الرجل على يديه إذا نهض في الصلاة وفي حديث وائل بن حجر في صفة صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : وإذا نهض نهض على ركبتيه واعتمد على فخذيه والحديث الترمذي عن أبي هريرة أن النبي كان ينهض في الصلاة على صدور قدميه. قال الترمذي : إن عليه العمل عند أهل العلم. وأما ما رواه البخاري عن مالك بن الحويرث أنه رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم إذا كان في وتر من صلاته لم ينهض حتى يستوي قاعداً فمحمول على حالة الكبر كما في الهداية، ويرد عليه أن هذا الحمل يحتاج إلى دليل وقد قال عليه الصلاة والسلام لمالك بن الحويرث لما أراد أن يفارقه : صلوا كما رأيتموني أصلي. ولم يفصل فكان الحديث حجة للشافعي، فالأولى أن يحمل على تعليم الجواز فلذا والله أعلم قال في الفتاوى الظهيرية قال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : إن الخلاف إنما هو في الأفضلية حتى لو فعل كما هو مذهب الشافعي لا بأس به عندنا اهـ. وكذا ترك الاعتماد مستحب لمن ليس به عذر عندنا على ما هو ظاهر كثير من الكتب المشهورة. قال الوبري : لا بأس بأن يعتمد براحتيه على الأرض عند النهوض من غير فصل بين العذر وعدمه. ومثله ما في المحيط عن الطحاوي: لا بأس بأن يعتمد بيديه على الأرض شيخاً كان أو شاباً. وهو قول عامة العلماء اهـ. والأوجه أن يكون سنة فتركه يكره تنزيهاً لما تقدم من النهي . وذكر الشارح أنه يكره تقديم إحدى الرجلين عند النهوض، ويستحب مراعاة الخلاف وهذا منه كما لا يخفى. نعم لو كان الدعاء المذكور منهياً . عنه عندنا لا تستحب المراعاة لما يلزم عليها من الخروج عن المذهب لكن ثبوت الكراهة يحتاج إلى دليل قوله: (فالأولى أن يحمل على تعليم الجواز قد يقال ينافي ذلك الحمل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام صلوا الخ) وفي النهر أقول : لا تنافي بين ما في الهداية وما قاله الحلواني بوجه إذ المدعي طلب النهوض وتركه يوجب خلاف الأولى وهو مرجع لا بأس به في أغلب استعماله، ولا ينافيه ما في المعراج أن جلسة الاستراحة مكروهة عندنا إذا المراد بها التنزيه، وكذا قول الطحاوي لا بأس بأن يعتمد الخ. فقوله في البحر الأوجه أن يكون سنة فيكره تركه» ممنوع قدم ذلك قريباً عند قول المتن أو بكور عمامته من أن مرجع خلاف الأولى كلا اهـ. والعجب أنه
His statement: (And he says the takbir for rising without support and sitting) The hadith of Abu Dawood: The Prophet forbade a man from placing his hands on the ground when rising in prayer. And in the hadith of Wail ibn Hajar describing the prayer of the Messenger of Allah: When he rose, he rose on his knees and supported himself on his thighs. And the hadith of Tirmidhi from Abu Hurayra: The Prophet used to rise in prayer on the soles of his feet. Tirmidhi said: This is acted upon by the people of knowledge. As for what Bukhari narrated from Malik ibn al-Huwayrith that he saw the Prophet, when in an odd rak'ah, not rise until he was sitting straight, it is interpreted as due to old age, as in al-Hidayah. But it is objected that this interpretation requires proof, and the Prophet said to Malik when he was about to leave: 'Pray as you have seen me pray,' without exception, so the hadith is proof for al-Shafi'i. Therefore it is better to interpret it as teaching permission. Hence, Allah knows best, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said in Fatawa al-Zahiriyya: The difference is only about preference; even if one does as the Shafi'i school holds, it is fine with us. Likewise, refraining from support is mustahab for one without excuse according to us, as is apparent in many well-known books. Al-Obari said: There is no problem with relying on one's palms on the ground when rising, without distinction between excuse or not. Similarly, in al-Muhit from al-Tahawi: There is no problem with relying on one's hands on the ground, whether old or young, and it is the saying of the general scholars. The more appropriate view is that it is sunnah, so leaving it is makruh tanzihi due to the prohibition mentioned. And the commentator mentioned that it is makruh tanzihi to put forward one foot when rising, and it is mustahab to observe the difference of opinion, and this is among them, as is not hidden. However, if the mentioned supplication is prohibited according to us, observing the difference is not mustahab because it would lead to leaving the school, but proving the karaha requires evidence. His statement: (It is better to interpret it as teaching permission, it may be said that this interpretation contradicts the Prophet's saying 'Pray...') And in al-Nahr I say: There is no contradiction between what is in al-Hidayah and what al-Halwani said at all, for what is intended is the request for rising and its leaving results in khilaf al-awla, and this does not contradict what is in al-Mi'raj that the sitting of rest is makruh according to us, if what is meant is tanzihi. Similarly, al-Tahawi's saying 'no problem with relying' etc. So his statement in al-Bahr that it is more appropriate to be sunnah and its abandonment is makruh is objectionable, as that was already stated near the text's statement 'or a corner of his turban' that the reference of khilaf al-awla is like that. Amazing!
Source pages p. 562

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on rising (al-nuhud) from prostration or sitting to stand for the next rak'ah. The Hanafi school holds that it is mustahab (recommended) to rise without using one's hands for support. The primary evidence is a hadith from Abu Dawood prohibiting a man from placing his hands on the ground when rising, and the hadith of Wail ibn Hajar describing the Prophet's practice of rising on his knees and using his thighs for support. The Shafi'i school, citing the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwayrith where the Prophet did not rise until fully seated, argues that the Prophet's command 'Pray as you have seen me pray' makes that practice obligatory. The Hanafi response, via al-Halwani, is that the difference is only in preference (afdaliyya), not in validity: if one uses hands, the prayer is still valid. The text also mentions al-Obari and al-Tahawi who consider reliance on hands permissible without any restriction. The overall preferred view in the Hanafi school (as per Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) is that rising without hands is sunnah, and doing otherwise is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked). The passage also notes the karaha of pushing forward one foot, and the recommendation of observing the difference of opinion (mura'at al-khilaf), which applies only if the alternative is not itself against the school.

Key Terms
الاعتماد (al-i'timad): Relying on the hands for support when rising in prayer
النهوض (al-nuhud): Rising from prostration or sitting to standing in prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on rising from prostration without relying on one's hands?
A) It is wajib
B) It is sunnah
C) It is haram
D) It is makruh tahrimi

Key Takeaway
Rising without hand support is the Hanafi sunnah; reliance is permissible but slightly disliked.

Exceptions in the Second Rak'ah: Omission of Opening Supplication, Ta'awwudh, and Raising Hands
Explaining the three differences between the first and second rak'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three exceptions in the second rak'ah according to the Hanafi school and explain the legal reasoning for each.

Core Idea
The second rak'ah mirrors the first except for three sunan omitted by design, not by oversight.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that the second rak'ah is identical to the first in essential obligations (arkan, wajibat, sunan) but has three deliberate omissions. The commentary unpacks the rationale behind each exception, rooted in Hanafi usul and hadith analysis, particularly the ongoing dispute about raising hands in prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base principle
Find the statement that the second rak'ah is like the first. Understand that this applies to all elements except those explicitly excluded.
The matn says 'al-thaniyah ka al-ula' meaning the second is like the first.
2
List the three exceptions
From the text, extract the three things omitted in the second rak'ah: opening supplication (istiftah), seeking refuge (ta'awwudh), and raising hands (except at specified places).
The text says 'illa annahu la yuthanni wa la yata'awwadhu wa la yarfa'u yadayhi'.
3
Analyze the legal cause for each exception
For each omission, identify the reason given in the commentary: istiftah is prescribed only at the start of the prayer; ta'awwudh is for the beginning of recitation; raf' al-yadayn is limited to the opening takbir because other instances were abrogated.
The commentary provides the 'illah (legal cause) for each omission.
4
Examine the dispute on raising hands
The text engages with the Shafi'i position that hands are raised at ruku etc. Follow the Hanafi response: the hadith of Ibn Umar is abrogated by later hadith (al-Bara', Jabir).
The passage discusses tarjih (preponderance) between conflicting narrations.
5
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis raise hands only at the opening takbir; Shafi'is raise at multiple points.
This ikhtilaf is a legitimate difference of ijtihad.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثانية كالأولى إلا أنه ليثني ولا يتعوذ ولا يرفع يديه إلا في فقعس معاذ قوله (والثانية كالأولى) أي فميا قدمناه الأركان من والواجبات والسنن الآداب إلا أنه لا يثنى) أي لا يأتي بدعاء الاستفتاح لأنه شرع في أول العبادة دون أثنائها ولذا دعاء الاستفتاح. قوله (ولا يتعوذ) لأنه شرع في أوّل القراءة لدفع الوسوسة فلا يتكرر إلا بتبدل المجلس كما لو تعوذ وقرأ ثم سكت قليلاً وقرأ، وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره ابن أمير حاج في شرحه من أنه ينبغي على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد أن يتعوذ في الثانية أيضاً لأنه سنة القراءة والقراءة تتجدد في كل ركعة لما علمت أنه سنة في أوّل القراءة. قوله : (ولا يرفع يديه إلا في فقعس صمعج) أي ولا يرفع يديه على وجه السنة المؤكدة إلا في هذه المواضع وليس مراده النفي مطلقاً لأن رفع الأيدي وقت الدعاء مستحب كما عليه المسلمون في سائر البلاد، فلا يرفع يديه عند الركوع ولا عند الرفع منه ولا في تكبيرات الجنائز لحديث أبي داود عن البراء قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يرفع يديه حين افتتح الصلاة ثم لم يرفعهما حتى انصرف ولحديث مسلم عن جابر ابن سمرة قال: خرج علينا رسول الله الله : فقال : ما لي أراكم رافعي أيديكم كأنها أذناب خيل شمس؟! تسكنوا في الصلاة. وشُمْس بضم المعجمة وسكون الميم جمع شَمُوس بفتحها، وضم الميم أي صعب. واعتراض البخاري في كتابه رفع اليدين بأن هذا الرفع كان في التشهد بدليل حديث عبد الله بن القبطية عن جابر أيضاً، رد بأن الظاهر أنهما حديثان لأن الذي يرفع يديه حال التسليم لا يقال له أسكن في الصلاة وبأن العبرة لعموم اللفظ وهو قوله اسكنوا في الصلاة لا لخصوص السبب وهو الإيماء حال التسليم. وفي فتح القدير: واعلم أن الآثار عن الصحابة والطرق عنه الله كثيرة جداً والكلام فيها واسع من جهة الطحاوي وغيره، والقدر المتحقق بعد ذلك كله ثبوت رواية كل من الأمرين عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام الرفع عند الركوع كما رواه الأئمة الستة في كتبهم عن ابن عمر، وعدمه كما رواه أبو داود وغير عن ابن مسعود وغيره فيحتاج إلى الترجيح ليقام التعارض. ويترجح ما صرنا إليه بأنه قد علم أنها كانت أقوال مباحة في الصلاة وأفعال من جنس هذا الرفع وقد علم نسخها فلا يبعد أن
And the second (rak'ah) is like the first except that he does not say the opening supplication, nor does he seek refuge, nor does he raise his hands except in [corrupted phrase]. His statement: (And the second is like the first) i.e., in what we have mentioned of arkan, wajibat, sunan, and adab, except that he does not say the opening supplication (istiftah), because it is prescribed at the beginning of the worship, not during it; hence the opening supplication. His statement: (Nor does he seek refuge) because it is prescribed at the beginning of the recitation to repel whisperings, so it is not repeated unless the gathering changes, such as if he sought refuge and recited, then paused briefly and recited. Thus what Ibn Amir Hajj mentioned in his commentary that according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad one should seek refuge in the second rak'ah as well because it is sunnah of recitation and recitation renews in every rak'ah, is refuted because it is sunnah at the start of recitation. His statement: (Nor does he raise his hands except in [corrupted]) means he does not raise his hands in the manner of emphasized sunnah except in these places; he does not intend absolute negation because raising hands at the time of supplication is mustahab as Muslims do in all lands. So he does not raise his hands at ruku, nor when straightening from it, nor in funeral takbirs, due to the hadith of Abu Dawood from al-Bara' who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah raise his hands when he started the prayer, then he did not raise them until he finished. And the hadith of Muslim from Jabir ibn Samura who said: The Messenger of Allah came out to us and said: 'Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be still in prayer.' 'Shums' is the plural of 'shamus' meaning difficult. And the objection of al-Bukhari in his book 'Raf' al-Yadayn' that this raising was in tashahhud based on the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Qibtiiyya from Jabir, is refuted because they are apparently two different hadiths, since the one who raises his hands at the time of taslim is not told 'be still in prayer', and because consideration is given to the general wording 'be still in prayer' not to the specific cause (signaling at taslim). In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the reports from the Companions and the ways regarding this are many, and discussion is extensive from al-Tahawi and others. What is established after all that is the confirmation of both narrations from him: raising at ruku as the six imams reported from Ibn Umar, and not raising as reported by Abu Dawood and others from Ibn Mas'ud, etc., so there is need for tarjih to resolve the apparent contradiction. What we have arrived at (Hanafi position) is preponderant because it is known that those were permissible sayings in prayer and actions of this sort of raising, and their abrogation is known, so it is not improbable that
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage explains the differences between the first and second rak'ah according to the Hanafi school. The matn states that the second rak'ah is like the first in arkan, wajibat, sunan, and adab, but with three exceptions: no opening supplication (istiftah), no seeking refuge (ta'awwudh), and no raising of hands except at the specified places (the opening takbir and according to some, the two 'Eid prayers). The commentary clarifies each exception: Istiftah is not repeated because it is prescribed only at the very beginning of the prayer. Ta'awwudh is not repeated because it is prescribed at the start of recitation; it is not tied to each rak'ah. Hence the objection of Ibn Amir Hajj is refuted. The third exception concerns raising hands: The Hanafi school holds that hands are raised only for the opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) and for the 'Eid takbirs, but not for ruku, standing from ruku, or funeral prayers. The text then engages in a long defense of the Hanafi position against the Shafi'i school, citing hadith from al-Bara' and Jabir ibn Samura. The opposition from al-Bukhari is answered. The passage concludes by noting that there are two conflicting sets of hadith (raising at ruku and not raising), and the Hanafi side is preponderant because the acts of raising at other points were later abrogated (naskh).

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands to the ears in prayer
دعاء الاستفتاح (du'a' al-istiftah): The opening supplication recited after the first takbir
التعوذ (al-ta'awwudh): Seeking refuge with Allah from the accursed Shaytan before reciting the Fatihah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT one of the exceptions in the second rak'ah?
A) No opening supplication
B) No ta'awwudh
C) No raising of hands except at the opening takbir
D) No recitation of Surah Fatihah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school teaches that the second rak'ah omits the opening supplication, ta'awwudh, and raising hands (except at the opening takbir) based on considered legal reasoning and preference of certain hadith.

The Three Exceptions of the Second Rak'ah and the Raising Hands Debate
Explains three exceptions of second rak'ah and disputes raising hands

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi exceptions of the second rak'ah, explain the acronym فقعس صمعج, and evaluate the Hanafi argument that raising hands at bowing is abrogated.

Core Idea
Raising hands at bowing is abrogated in the Hanafi school; the acronym فقعس صمعج encodes the only eight places where it remains sunna.

The second rak'ah mirrors the first in all rulings except three omissions: no thana', no ta'awwudh, and no raising of hands except in the specific places denoted by the acronym فقعس صمعج. The third exception triggers a major inter-madhhab dispute: does the sunna of raising hands extend to bowing and rising from bowing? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi argument that the practice was abrogated, supported by strong hadith and the famous debate between Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three exceptions
Read the first part of the passage and note the three actions omitted in the second rak'ah: thana', ta'awwudh, and raising hands except in specific places. Understand why each is omitted (thana' and ta'awwudh are only at the beginning of the prayer or recitation).
The matn states: 'The second is like the first except that he does not recite thana', does not seek refuge, and does not raise his hands except in فقعس صمعج.'
2
Decode the acronym فقعس صمعج
Break down the eight letters: ف (opening takbir), ق (qunut), ع (Eid), س (touching Black Stone), ص (Safa), م (Marwa), ع (Arafat), ج (jamarat). Three in prayer, five in Hajj. This encodes the only places where raising hands is an emphatic sunna.
The acronym is Hanafi-specific; other schools do not use it.
3
Understand the dispute over raising hands at bowing
The Shafi'i school holds it is sunna to raise hands at rukū' and raf' min rukū' based on hadith of Ibn Umar. The Hanafi school argues it was abrogated. Identify the opposing proof (Ibn Umar hadith) and the Hanafi proofs (hadith of al-Bara' and Jabir ibn Samurah).
The Hanafi response uses the principle that earlier permissible actions in prayer were abrogated by the command to 'be still'.
4
Analyze the abrogation argument
The passage argues that raising hands at bowing was part of the initial practice, then abrogated like other earlier permissible actions (e.g., speaking). The hadith 'be still in prayer' prohibits unnecessary movement. This is supported by qiyas: asl = abrogated actions, far' = raising hands, illa = both were permissible and then prohibited by the stillness command.
The commentator refutes al-Bukhari's objection that the hadith refers to taslim, using the generality of the word.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi: do not raise hands at bowing or rising. The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is clear: Hanafis do not raise at these points, Shafi'is do.
The famous debate between Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i in Makkah settled the issue for the Hanafi school, relying on the reliability of Hanafi narrators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعتماد وقعود والثانية كالأولى إلا أنه لاثني ولا يتعوذ ولا يرفع يديه إلا في فقعس صمعج سمي الهبوط باليمنى والنهوض بالشمال ولم يذكر للكراهة دليلاً وذكرها في المجتبى مروية عن بن جبل وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما قوله (والثانية كالأولى) أي فميا قدمناه الأركان من والواجبات والسنن الآداب إلا أنه لا يثنى) أي لا يأتي بدعاء الاستفتاح لأنه شرع في أول العبادة دون أثنائها ولذا دعاء الاستفتاح. قوله (ولا يتعوذ) لأنه شرع في أوّل القراءة لدفع الوسوسة فلا يتكرر إلا بتبدل المجلس كما لو تعوذ وقرأ ثم سكت قليلاً وقرأ، وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره ابن أمير حاج في شرحه من أنه ينبغي على قول أبي حنيفة ومحمد أن يتعوذ في الثانية أيضاً لأنه سنة القراءة والقراءة تتجدد في كل ركعة لما علمت أنه سنة في أوّل القراءة. قوله : (ولا يرفع يديه إلا في فقعس صمعج) أي ولا يرفع يديه على وجه السنة المؤكدة إلا في هذه المواضع وليس مراده النفي مطلقاً لأن رفع الأيدي وقت الدعاء مستحب كما عليه المسلمون في سائر البلاد، فلا يرفع يديه عند الركوع ولا عند الرفع منه ولا في تكبيرات الجنائز لحديث أبي داود عن البراء قال: رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يرفع يديه حين افتتح الصلاة ثم لم يرفعهما حتى انصرف ولحديث مسلم عن جابر ابن سمرة قال: خرج علينا رسول الله الله : فقال : ما لي أراكم رافعي أيديكم كأنها أذناب خيل شمس؟! تسكنوا في الصلاة. وشُمْس بضم المعجمة وسكون الميم جمع شَمُوس بفتحها، وضم الميم أي صعب. واعتراض البخاري في كتابه رفع اليدين بأن هذا الرفع كان في التشهد بدليل حديث عبد الله بن القبطية عن جابر أيضاً، رد بأن الظاهر أنهما حديثان لأن الذي يرفع يديه حال التسليم لا يقال له أسكن في الصلاة وبأن العبرة لعموم اللفظ وهو قوله اسكنوا في الصلاة لا لخصوص السبب وهو الإيماء حال التسليم. وفي فتح القدير: واعلم أن الآثار عن الصحابة والطرق عنه الله كثيرة جداً والكلام فيها واسع من جهة الطحاوي وغيره، والقدر المتحقق بعد ذلك كله ثبوت رواية كل من الأمرين عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام الرفع عند الركوع كما رواه الأئمة الستة في كتبهم عن ابن عمر، وعدمه كما رواه أبو داود وغير عن ابن مسعود وغيره فيحتاج إلى الترجيح لقيام التعارض. ويترجح ما صرنا إليه بأنه قد علم أنها كانت أقوال مباحة في الصلاة وأفعال من جنس هذا الرفع وقد علم نسخها فلا يبعد أن يكون هو أيضاً مشمولاً بالنسخ خصوصاً، وقد ثبت ما يعارضه ثبوتاً لا مرد له بخلاف عدمه فإنه لا يتطرق إليه احتمال عدم الشرعية لأنه ليس من جنس ما عهد فيه ذلك بل من جنس السكون الذي هو طريق ما أجمع على طلبه في الصلاة أعني الخشوع، وكذا بأفضلية الرواة عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و كل ما قاله أبو حنيفة للأوزاعي في الحكاية المشهورة عنهما. وأفاد بهذه الحروف سنية رفع اليدين في ثمانية مواضع: ثلاثة في الصلاة فالفاء لتكبيرة الافتتاح، والقاف للقنوت، والعين للعيدين. وخمسة في الحج فالسين عند استلام الحجر والصاد عند الصعود على الصفا، والميم للمروة، والعين لعرفات والجيم للجمرات، والرفع في الثلاثة الأول بحذاء الأذنين، وفي الخمسة تفصيل ففي استلام الحجر وعند الجمرتين الأولى والوسطى يرفع حذاء منكبيه ويجعل باطنهما نحو الكعبة في ظاهر الرواية وعند الصفا والمروة وبعرفات يرفعهما كالدعاء يديه نحو السماء. كذا في الفتاوى الظهيرية من المناسك قوله : (وإذا فرغ من سجدتي الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى فجلس عليها ونصب يمناه ووجه أصابعه نحو القبلة ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط أصابعه وهي تتورك وقرأ
The second is like the first except that he does not recite thana', does not seek refuge, and does not raise his hands except in the cases of فقعس صمعج (an acronym for certain positions). He descends with the right and rises with the left, and no proof of dislike is mentioned for that. It is mentioned in al-Mujtaba that it is narrated from Ibn Jabal and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them). His saying: 'The second is like the first' means in what we have presented of pillars, obligations, sunnas, and etiquettes, except that he does not recite thana' because it is legislated at the beginning of worship not in its middle, hence thana'' invocation. His saying: 'And does not seek refuge' because it is legislated at the beginning of recitation to repel whispers, so it is not repeated except with a change of assembly, as if he sought refuge and recited then paused briefly and recited again. By this, the objection of Ibn Amir Hajj in his commentary is repelled, who said it should be according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad that he seeks refuge in the second also because it is a sunna of recitation and recitation is renewed in each rak'ah, but we have understood that it is a sunna at the beginning of recitation. His saying: 'And does not raise his hands except in فقعس صمعج' means he does not raise his hands as an emphatic sunna except in these places. He does not intend absolute negation because raising hands during supplication is recommended as Muslims do in all lands. So he does not raise his hands at bowing, nor at rising from it, nor in the takbirs of funerals, due to the hadith of Abu Dawud from al-Bara' who said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) raise his hands when opening the prayer, then he did not raise them again until he finished. And the hadith of Muslim from Jabir ibn Samurah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) came out to us and said: 'Why do I see you raising your hands as if they are the tails of restive horses? Be still in prayer.' And 'shums' with a damma on the shin and sukun on the mim is the plural of 'shamus' meaning difficult. The objection of al-Bukhari in his book 'Raf' al-Yadayn' that this raising was during the tashahhud due to the hadith of Abdullah ibn al-Qibtiyya from Jabir is refuted by the fact that they are apparently two hadiths, and because the one who raises his hands during the taslim is not told 'be still in prayer', and the consideration is for the generality of the wording 'be still in prayer', not for the specific occasion of gesturing during the taslim. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that the narrations from the Companions and the paths from him (peace be upon him) are very many, and the discussion about them is extensive due to al-Tahawi and others. The certain reality after all that is the established transmission of both matters from him (peace be upon him): raising at bowing, as narrated by the six imams in their books from Ibn Umar, and absence of it as narrated by Abu Dawud and others from Ibn Mas'ud and others. So tarjeeh is needed due to conflict. Our view is preponderated because we know that these (former) rulings were permissible in prayer and actions of this type of raising, and we know their abrogation. So it is not far that this raising (at bowing) is also included in the abrogation specifially. And also due to the superiority of the narrators from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) and whatever Abu Hanifa said to al-Awza'i in the famous story about them. And with these letters, he indicated that raising hands is a sunna in eight places: three in prayer - the ف is for the opening takbir, the ق for qunut, the ع for the two Eids. And five in Hajj: the س for touching the Black Stone, the ص for ascending Safa, the م for Marwa, the ع for Arafat, and the ج for the jamarat. Raising in the former three is at the level of the ears. In the five, there is detail: when touching the Black Stone and at the first and second jamarat, he raises to the level of his shoulders and turns his palms towards the Ka'ba according to the apparent narration. When at Safa, Marwa, and Arafat, he raises them like supplication, his hands towards the sky. Thus in al-Fatawa al-Dhahiriyya from al-Manāsik. His saying: (When he finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects his right foot, and points his toes toward the qibla, and places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers while he is mutawarrik and he recites...
Source pages p. 563

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the ruling of the second rak'ah in prayer. It begins by stating that the second rak'ah is like the first in all pillars, obligations, sunnas, and etiquettes, with three exceptions: (1) no thana' (opening supplication), (2) no ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), and (3) no raising of hands except in specific places denoted by the acronym فقعس صمعج. The author explains that thana' is only recited at the beginning of the prayer, not in subsequent rak'ahs, and ta'awwudh is only recited at the beginning of recitation; it is not repeated unless a new assembly begins. Then the focus shifts to the third exception: raising hands. The commentator clarifies that the matn does not mean absolute prohibition of raising hands (since supplication with raised hands is recommended), but rather that the emphatic sunnah of raising hands at the opening takbir is not done in later rak'ahs except in eight specific places (three in prayer: opening takbir, qunut, and Eid; five in Hajj: touching the Black Stone, ascending Safa and Marwa, at Arafat, and at the jamarat). The passage then presents the inter-madhhab dispute over raising hands during bowing and rising from it. The Hanafi position is that this raising is abrogated, supported by hadiths from Abu Dawud and Muslim indicating the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not raise hands after the opening takbir. The commentator refutes objections and favors the Hanafi view by citing the abrogation argument and the superiority of narrators in the famous debate between Abu Hanifa and al-Awza'i. The acronym explanation at the end connects back to the Hanafi ruling that raising hands is only a sunna in those eight places, not in bowing or rising.

Key Terms
فقعس صمعج (faqaʿs ṣamʿaj): An acronym formed from eight letters indicating the eight places where raising hands is a sunnah: ف (opening takbir), ق (qunut), ع (Eid), س (touching Black Stone), ص (Safa), م (Marwa), ع (Arafat), ج (jamarat).
رفع اليدين (rafʿ al-yadayn): The act of raising both hands during prayer; the discussion centers on whether it is a sunnah only at the opening takbir or also at bowing and rising.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation; the ruling of an earlier revealed ruling is superseded by a later one. In this context, the earlier practice of raising hands at bowing is abrogated by the command 'be still in prayer'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following situations is it a sunnah to raise the hands during prayer?
A) At the opening takbir and at bowing
B) At the opening takbir, qunut, and the two Eid prayers
C) At every takbir
D) Only at the opening takbir

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits raising hands as an emphatic sunna only in eight specific places (encoded in the acronym فقعس صمعج); raising at bowing is abrogated, a position supported by hadith and the authority of Abu Hanifa's debate with al-Awza'i.

Sitting Posture After the Second Rak'ah: Iftirash and Tawarruk
Describes the recommended sitting posture, foot placement, and hand position after the second rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sunnah sitting posture for tashahhud according to the Hanafi school, distinguish between iftirash and tawarruk, and apply the ruling to both fard and nafl prayers.

Core Idea
The sunnah after every two rak'ahs is to sit on the left foot with right foot erect; tawarruk is permissible but not preferred.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the commentator explains the recommended sitting posture during tashahhud, supported by the hadith of Aisha. We will examine the posture, its proof, and the scope of its application across obligatory and supererogatory prayers, as well as the permissibility of alternative postures like tawarruk.

Guided Path
1
Identify the posture
Read the matn's description: spreading the left foot and sitting on it, erecting the right foot, pointing toes to the qibla, placing hands on thighs with spread fingers. This is iftirash.
Tawarruk is a variant where one sits on the hip with left foot tucked under the right leg.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentator cites the hadith of Aisha (Muslim) that the Prophet used this posture after every two rak'ahs. This is the proof for the sunnah.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala) in establishing the practice.
3
Understand the scope
The matn says 'al-salat' which is general. The commentator emphasizes that this applies to both fard and nafl, contra al-Mujtaba's restriction to fard.
Nafl is based on ease, but the sunnah remains the described posture.
4
Distinguish iftirash and tawarruk
Iftirash is the sunnah; tawarruk is permissible (ja'iz) but not preferred. The commentator notes that if one sits mutawarrik, it is allowed.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i school which recommends tawarruk in the final tashahhud.
5
Resolve hand placement dispute
The matn says place hands on thighs (fakhd) with spread fingers. The commentator refutes al-Tahawi's view that hands go on knees with separated fingers, citing the hadith of Ibn Umar.
The sunnah is to place hands on the thighs, not the knees.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا فرغ من سجدتي الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى فجلس عليها ونصب يمناه ووجه أصابعه نحو القبلة ووضع يديه على فخذيه وبسط أصابعه وهي تتورك وقرأ لحديث مسلم عن عائشة : كان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول في كل ركعتين ،التحية، وكان يفترش رجله اليسرى وينصب اليمني وهذا بيان السنة عندنا حتى لو تورك جاز. أطلق الصلاة فشمل الفرض والنفل فيقعد فيهما على هذه الكيفية ففي المجتبى ناقلاً عن صلاة الجلابي أن هذا في الفرض وفي النفل يقعد كيف شاء كالمريض مخالف لإطلاق الكتب المعتبرة المشهورة. نعم النفل مبناه على التخفيف ولذا يجوز قاعداً مع القدرة على القيام لكن الكلام إنما هو في السنية . قوله: (ووضع يديه على فخديه وبسط أصابعه يعني وضع يده اليمنى على فخذه اليمنى ويده اليسرى على فخذه اليسرى لحديث مسلم عن ابن عمر مرفوعاً كذلك أشار إلى رد ما ذكره الطحاوي أنه يضع يديه على ركبتيه ويفرق بين أصابعه كحالة الركوع لحديث مسلم
And when he finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects his right foot, and points his toes toward the qibla, and places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers while he is mutawarrik and he recites. Due to the hadith of Muslim from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) used to recite the tashahhud after every two rak'ahs, and he would spread his left foot and erect his right. This is the explanation of the sunnah according to us, so much so that if he performs tawarruk, it is permissible. The ruling is general for both obligatory and supererogatory prayers; he sits in this manner in both. In al-Mujtaba, quoting from Salat al-Jullabi, it is said this is for obligatory prayer, and in supererogatory he sits however he wishes like a sick person, contravening the general scope of the reliable and well-known books. Yes, supererogatory prayer is based on ease, hence it is permissible to sit even if able to stand, but the discussion is about sunnah. His saying: (And he places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers) means he places his right hand on his right thigh and his left hand on his left thigh, due to the marfu' hadith of Muslim from Ibn Umar. This indicates a refutation of what al-Tahawi mentioned that he places his hands on his knees and separates his fingers like the state of bowing, due to the hadith of Muslim.
Source pages p. 564

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended sitting posture after the second rak'ah during tashahhud. The matn states: 'he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects his right foot, and points his toes toward the qibla, and places his hands on his thighs and spreads his fingers.' The commentator provides the proof from a hadith of Aisha in Muslim that the Prophet used this posture after every two rak'ahs. This sunnah applies to both obligatory (fard) and supererogatory (nafl) prayers, although some later sources (like al-Mujtaba) restrict it to fard, but the commentator dismisses that as contrary to the established texts. For nafl, ease is allowed, but the sunnah remains the described posture. The hand placement is specifically on the thighs (fakhd), not on the knees as claimed by al-Tahawi; the hadith of Ibn Umar supports the thigh placement with fingers spread. The commentator notes that if one sits mutawarrik (buttocks on the floor, left foot tucked under right calf and right foot erected), it is permissible, but the sunnah is iftirash (sitting on the left foot).

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirāsh): The posture of sitting on the left foot, with the right foot erect and toes pointing toward the qibla.
تورك (tawarruk): Sitting with the left hip on the floor, left foot tucked under the right leg, and right foot erect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The right foot is erected with toes pointing toward the qibla
C) The right foot is tucked under the left leg
D) The right foot is crossed over the left

Key Takeaway
The sunnah after every two rak'ahs is to sit on the left foot (iftirash) with the right foot erect; tawarruk is permissible but not preferred, and this applies to both fard and nafl prayers.

Finger Placement and Pointing During Tashahhud: Hanafi Rulings and Dispute
Hanafi rulings on finger positions and the dispute over pointing during tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on pointing the index finger during tashahhud and explain the disagreement within the school regarding the method of finger placement.

Core Idea
The mufta bihi in Hanafi fiqh is to point with the index finger while gripping the other fingers in the 'aqd thalathah wa khamsin grip.

The manner of holding one's hand during tashahhud has been a subject of discussion among Hanafi jurists. While some early authorities cautioned against pointing the index finger due to the principle of stillness in prayer, later scholars, supported by hadith evidence, have recommended a specific grip with pointing. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the preferred position and addresses the intra-madhhab differences.

Guided Path
1
State the act and its context
Identify that we are discussing the hand position during tashahhud in salah. Note that there are several components: finger placement on the knee, whether to point the index finger, and how to grip the other fingers.
The act is from the sunan of prayer.
2
Identify the two main positions
One position (early scholars) holds that one should not point the index finger; rather, the fingers are spread and kept still. The other (later scholars) holds that one should point with a specific grip (the 'aqd thalathah wa khamsin).
The dispute is within the Hanafi school itself.
3
Examine the proofs for each view
The anti-pointing view argues from the principle that prayer is based on stillness (sukun). The pro-pointing view cites the practice of Ibn Umar, a hadith in Sahih Muslim, and reports from Abu Hanifa that pointing is sunna.
Evidence is primarily hadith and practice of the Salaf.
4
Follow the tarjih process
The later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) like the author of Fath al-Qadir and al-Bahr al-Ra'iq weighed the evidence and concluded that the hadith evidence is stronger and that the stillness is not violated. They also noted that the majority of Hanafi texts support pointing with grip.
Tarjih is based on strength of dalil and consensus of later authorities.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative ruling for fatwa is to point the index finger while gripping the little finger, ring finger, and thumb together, with the middle finger forming a ring with the thumb. This is the 'aqd thalathah wa khamsin.
This is the position relied upon in fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وعلل له في البدائع بأنه على الكيفية الأولى تكون الأصابع متوجهة إلى القبلة وعلى الثانية إلى الأرض لكنه لا يتم إلا إذا كانت الأصابع عطفت على الركبة، أما إذا كانت رؤوسها عند رأس الركبة فلا يتم الترجيح. واعترض في المجموع قولهم كعاقد ثلاثة وخمسين فإن شرطه عند أهل الحساب أن الخنصر على البنصر وليس مراداً بل هو أن يضعها على الراحة كا نصر التي يستمونها تسعة وخمسين ولم ينطقوا بها تبعاً للخبر. وأجاب في الإقليد أن عبرة وضع الخنصر على البنصر في عقد ثلاثة وخمسين هي طريقة أقباط مصر ولم يعتبر غيرهم فيها ذلك. وقال في الكفاية : عدم اشتراط ذلك طريقة المتقدمين .اهـ. وقال ابن الفركاح: إن عدم الاشتراط طريقة لبعض الحساب وعليه يكون تسعة وخمسون هيئة أخرى أو تكون الهيئة الواحدة تشترك بين العددين فيحتاج إلى قرينة اهـ. قال الحلبي في شرح منية المصلي : وصفتها أن يحلق من يده اليمنى عند الشهادة الإبهام والوسطى ويقبض البنصر الخنصر ويضع رأس إبهامه على حرف المفصل الأوسط ويرفع الأصبع . عند النفي ويضعها عند الإثبات ويكره أن يشير بكلتا مسبحتيه قوله : (لكنه لا يتم الخ) قال في النهر : لا يخفى أن وضع اليدين عليها يستلزمه قوله : ( ورجح في فتح القدير القول بالإشارة) أي مع قبض الأصابع كما . هو صريح عبارة الفتح، وبه صرح في منية المصلي حيث قال : فإن أشار يعقد الخنصر والنبصر ويحلق الوسطى بالإبهام ويقيم السبابة .اهـ. فالإشارة إنما هي على كيفية خاصة عندنا وهي العقد المذكور كما هو المذكور في عامة الكتب كالبدائع والنهاية والمعراج وشروح المنية والقهستاني والنهر والظهيرية وشرح النقاية وغيرها. وأما ما نقله في الشرنبلالية عن البرهان من أنه يشير ولا. [ثم من صفحة 566] يعقدهو قول ثالث لم أر من عول عليه ولا من نقله سواه، فالعمل على ما في كتب المذهب من القولين: أحدهما وهو المشهور بسط الأصابع بلا إشارة، والثاني الذي رجحه المتأخرون عقد الأصابع عند الإشارة. وأما ما نقله في الدر المختار عن دور البحار وشرحه موافقاً لما نقله الشرنبلالي عن البرهان فغير صحيح فإني راجعت درر البحار وشرحه المسمى غرر الأفكار فرأيت فهما أن الفتوى على الإشارة مع العقد، وقد أوضحت هذه المسألة بنقولها المعتبرة في رسالة سميتها «رفع التردد في
Also from Ibn 'Umar: he added, 'and he made a grip of three and fifty and pointed with the index finger.' He preferred the first method, saying: 'He does not take hold of the knee; that is the most correct.' Thus the second method in the hadith is interpreted as permissible, and the first as explaining the preferable. In al-Bada'i' it is reasoned that in the first method the fingers face the qibla, in the second they face the ground, but this is not complete unless the fingers are bent over the knee; if their tips are at the top of the knee, the preference is not complete. According to the third method from Muhammad in Jami' al-Tafariq, the fingertips are at the knee. In al-Mujtaba, he indicated that spreading the fingers means not pointing the index finger during the two shahadas, and this is the view of many shaykhs. In al-Wilwaljiyya and al-Tanqih: the fatwa is on this, because prayer is based on stillness, and it is disliked in Munyat al-Musalli. In Fath al-Qadir, he preferred the view of pointing, and that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa as Muhammad said; the view of not pointing contradicts transmission and reason, and it is reported in Sahih Muslim from his action. In al-Mujtaba: since the narrations from all our companions agree that it is sunna, and likewise from the Kufans and Medinese, and the abundance of hadiths and reports, acting upon it is preferable. He said (the author's text): 'And he made a grip of three and fifty.' Al-Ramli said: 'By placing the thumb under the index finger on the edge of the palm.' Muslim narrated from Ibn al-Zubayr 'like one making a grip of three and twenty.' Al-Khatib al-Shirbini in Sharh al-Minhaj: the jurists expressed the first without the second following Ibn 'Umar's narration. An objection in al-Majmu' to their saying 'like one making a grip of three and fifty' because its condition with arithmeticians is that the little finger be over the ring finger, but that is not intended; rather it is to place it on the palm like the fingers that they call nine and fifty, but they did not utter it following the report. In al-Iqlid he answered that the consideration of placing the little finger on the ring finger in the grip of three and fifty is the method of the Copts of Egypt, and others did not consider that. In al-Kifaya: not stipulating that is the method of the early scholars. Ibn al-Firkah said: 'Not stipulating it is the method of some arithmeticians, and accordingly nine and fifty is another form, or the single form is shared between the two numbers, so a context is needed.' Al-Halabi in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli said: 'Its description is that he makes a ring of his right hand at the shahada with the thumb and middle finger, clenches the ring finger and little finger, places the tip of his thumb on the edge of the middle joint, and raises the finger at negation and places it at affirmation, and it is disliked to point with both index fingers.' He said: 'But it is not complete...' In al-Nahr: 'It is not hidden that placing the two hands on them necessitates it.' He said: 'And in Fath al-Qadir he preferred the view of pointing, meaning with clenching the fingers, as is clear from Fath's expression. In Munyat al-Musalli he stated: 'If he points, he clenches the little finger and ring finger, makes a ring of the middle finger with the thumb, and raises the index finger.' Thus pointing is only according to a specific method in our school, which is the mentioned grip, as is mentioned in most books like al-Bada'i', al-Nihaya, al-Mi'raj, the commentaries of al-Munya, al-Qahistani, al-Nahr, al-Zahiriyya, Sharh al-Niqaya, etc. As for what is narrated in al-Shurnublaliyya from al-Burhan that he points without [gripping], it is a third view that I have not seen anyone rely upon nor anyone transmit besides him. So the practice is based on the two views in the school: one of them, which is famous, is spreading the fingers without pointing, and the second, which the later scholars preferred, is gripping the fingers at the time of pointing. As for what is narrated in al-Durr al-Mukhtar from Durar al-Bihar and its commentary, agreeing with what al-Shurnublali narrated from al-Burhan, it is incorrect, for I have checked Durar al-Bihar and its commentary named Ghurar al-Afkar and saw in both that the fatwa is on pointing with the grip. I have clarified this issue with its reliable narrations in a treatise I named 'Raf' al-Taraddud fi'.
Source pages p. 565

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the manner of holding the fingers and whether to point the index finger during tashahhud. The author presents three methods of finger placement: (1) placing the fingers on the knee and pointing with the index finger, (2) a similar method but with fingers touching the knee differently, and (3) the method from Muhammad that the fingertips are at the knee. The dispute centers on whether pointing the index finger is sunna or makruh. Some earlier scholars like those in al-Wilwaljiyya and al-Tanqih held it makruh because prayer requires stillness. However, later scholars like the author of Fath al-Qadir preferred pointing, citing reports from Abu Hanifa and hadith from Sahih Muslim. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq supports the later view, stating that the fatwa is on pointing with a specific finger grip (the so-called 'aqd thalathah wa khamsin) where the thumb is placed under the index finger, the middle finger forms a ring with the thumb, and the ring and little fingers are clenched. He refutes a third view reported from al-Burhan that one points without any finger grip, considering it unreliable. The mufta bihi position according to the later scholars is to point while gripping the fingers as described.

Key Terms
عقد ثلاثة وخمسين ('aqd thalathah wa khamsin): A specific way of holding the fingers during tashahhud where the little finger is placed on the ring finger, and the thumb is placed under the index finger, making a grip resembling the number 53 in finger counting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on pointing the index finger during tashahhud?
A) It is makruh because prayer requires stillness.
B) It is sunna and should be done with a specific finger grip.
C) It is wajib and must be done with the index finger only.
D) It is mubah and there is no specific method.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi is to point the index finger during tashahhud while gripping the other fingers in the 'aqd thalathah wa khamsin method, as this combines the stronger hadith evidence with the school's later consensus.
