Rulings on Forgetting the Left Taslim and Volume of the Second Taslim
Rulings on forgetfulness in taslim and volume of second taslim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rulings for forgetting the left taslim and determine the correct volume for the second taslim.

Core Idea
Forgetting the left taslim requires returning to sit if you haven't left; the second taslim should be audible to inform followers.

The commentary expands on two practical issues: what to do if you forget the left taslim and whether the second taslim should be loud or soft. These details ensure the prayer is completed in accordance with the sunnah and the needs of the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario for forgetfulness
The case: someone says the right taslim, forgets the left, and stands up. What must he do?
The text says he should return and sit to say the left taslim as long as he hasn't spoken or left the mosque.
2
Determine the limits of returning
He may return only if he has not spoken or exited the mosque. If he has, the left taslim is no longer required.
This restricts the obligation to return.
3
Analyze the volume dispute
Some scholars say the second taslim should be softer (or silent), others say it should be audible but less than the first. The text says the correct view is that it should be audible so followers know the imam is not doing sajda al-sahw.
The preferred view: second taslim audible, but not as loud as the first.
4
Apply the rule for exiting prayer
Exiting prayer requires the full phrase 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'; saying just 'al-salam' is insufficient for someone joining.
This is from the nawazil discussion.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله عن يمينه ويساره بيان للسنة ورد على مالك القائل بأنه يسلم تسليمة تلقاء وجهه ولو بدأ باليسار عامداً أو ناسياً فإنه يسلم عن يمينه ولا يعيده على يساره ولا شيء عليه، ولو سلم تلقاء وجهه فإنه يسلم عن يساره. ولو سلم عن يمينه ونسي عن يساره حتى قام فإنه يرجع ويقعد ويسلم ما لم يتكلم أو يخرج من المسجد. وفي المجتبى : ولم يذكر قدر ما يحول به وجهه وقد ورد في حديث ابن مسعود أنه كان قوله : (أن تكون الثانية أخفض من (الأولى) قال في المنية : ومن المشايخ من قال يخفض الثانية . قال الحلبي : وكأن مراده أنه يخفيها ولا يجهر بها أصلاً لما قلنا من عدم الاحتياج إلى الجهر أي لأن المقصود بالجهر الإعلام وقد حصل بالأولى. وهذا بخلاف القول الأول لأن ظاهره أنه يجهر بها دون الجهر بالأولى والأصح القول الأول لأن الأولى وإن دلت على تعقيب الثانية إياها إلا أن المقتدين ينتظرون الإمام فيها ولا يعلمون أنه يأتي بها أو يسجد قبلها السهو حصل له . قوله: (ولا شيء عليه ولو سلم عن يمينه كذا في النسخ. وفي بعضها زيادة وهي : ولو سلم تلقاء وجهه فإنه يسلم عن يساره ولو سلم الخ. قوله : (أو يخرج من المسجد قال في النهر : والصحيح أنه إن استدبر القبلة لا يسلم عن يمينه حتى يرى بياض خده الأيمن، وعن يساره حتى يرى بياض خده الأيسر . وفي النوازل: لو قال «السلام» ودخل في الصلاة لا يكون داخلاً فثبت أن الخروج لا يتوقف على «عليكم».
His statement: 'To his right and left' is an explanation of the sunnah and a refutation of Malik who says that one says one taslim facing the front. If one begins with the left intentionally or forgetfully, he then says the salam to his right and does not repeat it to his left and nothing is upon him. If one says the salam facing the front, he then says it to his left. If one says the salam to his right and forgets the left until he stands up, he returns and sits and says the salam as long as he has not spoken or left the mosque. In al-Mujtaba: The extent of turning his face is not mentioned; it has come in the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud that he used to... (above). He said in al-Munya: Some mashayikh said he lowers the second. al-Halabi said: It seems he means that he conceals it and does not utter it aloud at all, because we said there is no need for loudness, meaning the purpose of loudness is notification and it has been achieved by the first. This is contrary to the first statement because its apparent meaning is that he says it aloud but not as loud as the first; the correct view is the first because the first, even though it indicates the second's following it, the followers are waiting for the imam in it and do not know whether he performs it or does sajda al-sahw before it. So he must make them hear it. His statement: 'And nothing is upon him even if he says salam to his right' — thus in the copies. In some there is an addition: 'And if he says salam facing the front, then he says salam to his left; and if he says salam etc.' His statement: 'Or leaves the mosque' — he said in al-Nahr: The correct view is that if he turns his back to the qibla, he does not say salam to his right until he sees the whiteness of his right cheek, and to his left until he sees the whiteness of his left cheek. In al-Nawazil: If he says 'al-salam' and enters into the prayer, he does not become inside; thus it is established that exiting does not depend on 'alaykum'.
Source pages p. 580

Commentary
This portion of the commentary elaborates on the direction and order of the taslim. The matn's phrase 'to his right and left' indicates the sunnah method, countering Imam Malik who held that only one taslim to the front is required. If a person mistakenly starts with the left, he should still perform the right taslim and not repeat the left. If one only says one taslim facing forward, then he should still say the left taslim. Forgetting the left taslim after standing up requires returning to sit and perform it, provided he hasn't spoken or left the mosque. The text also discusses the volume of the second taslim: some scholars say it should be softer, others say it should be audible but less than the first. The correct view is that it should be audible so that followers know the imam is not doing sajda al-sahw. Additionally, if someone says only 'al-salam' (without 'alaykum') and someone else tries to join the prayer, he does not become part of the prayer, showing that exiting prayer requires the full phrase.

Key Terms
تسليمة (taslima): One utterance of the salam at the end of prayer.
جهر (jahr): Audibility; here referring to how loudly the second taslim is said.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the correct ruling on the volume of the second taslim?
A) It should be silent.
B) It should be as loud as the first.
C) It should be audible but softer than the first.
D) It should be inaudible.

Key Takeaway
Forgetfulness of the left taslim requires returning to sit if you haven't spoken or left; the second taslim should be audible to inform followers.

Intention in the Closing Salam: Whom Should You Greet?
Explaining the sunnah intention in taslim and the dispute over whom to greet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on intention in taslim and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whom to intend.

Core Idea
In the closing salam, intend only those praying with you — the sunnah is specific to the qawm.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq explains the sunnah of having intention in the closing salam and addresses a significant intra-Hanafi dispute: should you intend only those in prayer (the qawm) or everyone in the mosque? The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents the majority view corrected by Shams al-A'imma and rebuts alternatives. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate rivayat and follow the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its sunnah status
First, recognize that the act under discussion is the intention (niyyah) in the closing salam. The text states it is sunnah, not wajib. Understanding this sets the hukm level.
Sunnah here means a recommended practice; its omission does not invalidate the salah.
2
Understand the hadith evidence
Locate the dalil from Sahih Muslim about greeting 'brother on right and left'. Al-Nawawi explains that 'brother' refers to those present in the prayer. This supports the view that the salam is directed to fellow worshippers, not all believers.
The phrase 'brother' is key to understanding the scope of the greeting.
3
Distinguish the majority view from the opposing view
The majority (Shams al-A'imma, the author) holds that one should intend only those in prayer (the qawm). The opposing view, found in al-Khulasah and attributed to al-Hakim al-Shahid, says to intend all in the mosque, analogizing to tashahhud and the returning traveler.
The opposing view is considered weak in this text.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if you intend only the qawm, women and absentees are excluded; if you intend all in the mosque, they are included. This affects reward and completeness of the sunnah.
The dispute also affects women's inclusion in the greeting.
5
Apply the mufta bihi
The relied position is to intend only those in prayer with you. When performing the salam, make the niyyah for the qawm. This aligns with the hadith and the correction of Shams al-A'imma.
For the follower, the intention is independent of the imam's intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله مع الإمام بيان للأفضل يعني الأفضل للمأموم المقارنة في التحريمة والسلام عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما الأفضل عدمها للاحتياط، وله أن الاقتداء عقد موافقة وإنها في القرآن لا في التأخير. وإنما شبه السلام بالتحريمة لأن المقارنة في التحريمة باتفاق الروايات عن أبي حنيفة، وأما في السلام ففيه روايتان لكن الأصح ما في الكتاب كما في الخلاصة. وقوله ناوياً القوم بيان للأفضل لما في صحيح مسلم عنه : «أما يكفي أحدكم يضع يده على فخذه ثم يسلم على أخيه عن يمينه وعن شماله (۱) قال النووي في شرحه : أن المراد بالأخ الجنس من إخوانه الحاضرين عن اليمين والشمال ويزاد عليه من كان أمامه أو وراءه بالدلالة لأن المقصود من ذلك مزيد التودد . وأما ما عللوا به من أنه لما اشتغل بمناجاة ربه صار بمنزلة الغائب عن الخلق وعند التحلل يصير خارجاً فيسلم كمسافر قدم من سفره فلا يفيد الاقتصار على من معه في الصلاة بل يعم الحاضرين مصلياً أو غيره. وإنما احتيج إلى النية لأنه مقيم للسنة فينويها كسائر السنن وكذا ذكر شيخ الإسلام أنه إذا سلم أحد خارج الصلاة ينوي السنة وخالف صدر الإسلام فقال : لا حاجة للإمام إلى النية في السلام آخر الصلاة لأنه يجهر بالسلام ويشير إليهم فهو فوق النية، ورد بأن الجهر للإعلام بالخروج والنية لإقامة السنة . وأراد بالقوم من كان معه في الصلاة فقط وهو قول الجمهور وصححه شمس الأئمة بخلاف سلام التشهد فإنه ينوي جميع المؤمنين والمؤمنات، فما في الخلاصة من أن الصحيح أنه ينوي من كان معه أنه في المسجد ضعيف وكذا ما اختاره الحاكم الشهيد من كسلام التشهد . وزاد السروجي: وأنه ينوي المؤمنين من الجن أيضاً. وخرج بذكر القوم النساء ولهذا قالوا: النساء ينوي في زماننا لعدم حضورهن الجماعة أو لكراهيته لكن ذكر محمد في الأصل أنه ينوي الرجال والنساء، وفي الحقيقة لا اختلاف فما في الأصل مبني على حضورهن الجماعة، يأتي به. كذا في القنية قوله : (لا يكون داخلاً) أي لو اقتدى به إنسان بعد قوله: «السلام» قبل أن يقول «عليكم» لا يصير داخلاً في صلاته لأنه اقتداء بغير مصل قوله : (فما في الخلاصة من أن الصحيح الخ) قال في النهر : يمكن تخريج ما في الخلاصة على الراجح ولفظه وينوي من في المسجد هو الصحيح فعلى هذا لا ينوي النساء في زماننا .اهـ. إذ المعنى من معه في الصلاة كائناً في المسجد بدليل ما بعده وهذا أولى من الجزم بضعفه. قوله : (وخرج بذكر القوم النساء) بناء على أن كان معه.
His statement: 'With the imam' is an explanation of the preferred (afdal): it means the preferred for the follower (ma'mum) is to perform the takbirat al-tahrimah and salam simultaneously with the imam according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the preferred is not to do so for caution. His reasoning is that following (iqtida') is a contract of agreement, and it lies in alignment (quran) not delay. He likened the salam to the tahrimah because simultaneity in tahrimah is agreed upon in rivayat from Abu Hanifa; regarding salam, there are two rivayat, but the correct is what is in the book (matn) as in al-Khulasah. His statement: 'Intending the people (qawm)' is an explanation of the preferred due to what is in Sahih Muslim from him: 'Is it not sufficient for one of you to place his hand on his thigh then say salam to his brother on his right and left?' (1). al-Nawawi said in his commentary: What is meant by 'brother' is the genus of his brothers, the ones present on the right and left, and added to them those in front and behind by indication, because the purpose is increased affection. As for their reasoning that when he was occupied with his private conversation with his Lord, he became like one absent from creation, and at the time of leaving (the prayer) he becomes an outsider and says salam like a traveler returning from his journey, it does not benefit restricting it to those in prayer with him; rather it includes all those present, whether praying or not. The need for intention (niyyah) is because he is performing a sunnah, so he intends it like other sunan. Similarly, Shaykh al-Islam mentioned that if one says salam outside prayer, he intends the sunnah. Sadr al-Islam opposed, saying there is no need for the imam to intend in the salam at the end of prayer because he says it aloud and points to them, which is above intention. It was refuted that the loudness is to announce the ending, and the intention is to establish the sunnah. He intended by 'qawm' only those who were in prayer with him, and this is the view of the majority and was corrected by Shams al-A'imma, contrary to the salam of tashahhud, where he intends all believing men and women. So what is in al-Khulasah that the correct is that he intends those with him in the mosque is weak, as is what al-Hakim al-Shahid chose, resembling the salam of tashahhud. al-Saruji added: that he also intends the believing jinn. By mentioning 'qawm', women are excluded; thus they said: women intend in our time due to their lack of attending congregation or due to its dislike, but Muhammad mentioned in al-Asl that he intends men and women. In reality there is no disparity; what is in al-Asl is based on their attending congregation; it is to be acted upon. Likewise in al-Qunyah. His statement: (He does not become inside) meaning if a person followed him after he said 'al-salam' before saying 'alaykum', he does not become inside his prayer because following a non-praying person. His statement: (So what is in al-Khulasah that the correct is... etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is possible to derive what is in al-Khulasah from the preponderant view, and its wording is: 'and he intends those in the mosque is the correct view'; on this basis, he does not intend women in our time. The meaning is 'those with him in prayer wherever in the mosque' as evidenced by what follows; this is better than categorically declaring it weak. His statement: (By mentioning 'qawm' women are excluded) is based on what was with him.
Source pages p. 581

Commentary
This passage discusses the intention (niyyah) during the closing salam. First, it states the intra-Hanafi preference: Abu Hanifa holds that the follower should say the salam simultaneously with the imam, while the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) prefer delay for caution. The text then focuses on the intention in the salam: the sunnah is to intend the 'qawm' (those praying with you) when saying the salam. A hadith from Sahih Muslim supports greeting 'brothers' on right and left, which al-Nawawi interprets as all present, including those in front and behind. The intention is needed because one is performing a sunnah. There is a dispute: some scholars like Sadr al-Islam think no intention is needed due to the loudness and gesture, but the refutation clarifies that loudness is for announcement, intention for sunnah. The majority view, corrected by Shams al-A'imma, is to intend only those in prayer, not all in the mosque (as in al-Khulasah) nor like the tashahhud salam (which includes all believers). Some scholars add intending jinn, and there is nuance regarding women: Muhammad's al-Asl includes women, but the later view excludes them in our time due to non-attendance. The text reconciles this: if women attend, they are included.

Key Terms
القوم (al-qawm): The people praying with the imam (those in the same salah).
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The guardian angels (kiraman katibin).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (as corrected by Shams al-A'imma), whom should the worshipper intend when saying the closing salam?
A) All believers, living and dead
B) Only those in prayer with him (the qawm)
C) Everyone in the mosque
D) Only the angels

Key Takeaway
In the closing salam, the sunnah is to intend only those who are praying with you (the qawm), based on the hadith and the correction of Shams al-A'imma.

The Departure of the Recording Angels: An Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Explores ikhtilaf on the recording angels' departure

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the different scholarly opinions on whether the angel of sins departs during specific states and evaluate the evidence from a Hanafi perspective.

Core Idea
Does the angel of sins leave during defecation, intercourse, or prayer? The answer is disputed, and the Hanafi view requires strong evidence.

This lesson delves into the nuanced discussions regarding the two recording angels (al-malakan al-katiban). The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents multiple opinions on whether these angels, particularly the one recording sins, depart during certain acts. We will explore the evidence cited by each side and understand the Hanafi stance on this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issues
List the three main points of disagreement: whether the recording angels change at day/night, where they sit, and whether the angel of sins leaves during defecation, intercourse, and prayer.
2
Examine the different positions
Note the proponents of each view: majority (jumhur) say they change, others say they do not; some place them in the mouth, others on the right/left; and the departure is said by some scholars including al-Qurtubi.
The author reports these without fully endorsing any.
3
Analyze the key evidence
Focus on the hadith cited: the hadith about angels alternating, the hadith about cleaning the mouth, and the hadith about spitting in prayer. Understand how each side uses these proofs.
The author questions the strength of some evidence.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques the claim of departure, noting weak transmission and alternative interpretations. The Hanafi school tends to reject the departure view as unproven.
The author calls for caution and further reflection.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If the angel of sins leaves, a person may be less vigilant; if they remain, accountability is continuous. The Hanafi view upholds constant recording.
This affects one's state of mind in acts like prayer and using the toilet.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
وعشرون ألفاً، والرسل ثلاثمائة وثلاثة عشر جماً غفيراً. كذا في الكشاف في سورة الحج لكن لما كان ظنياً لأنه خبر واحد لم يعارض قوله تعالى ورسلاً قد قصصناهم عليك من قبل ورسلاً لم نقصصهم عليك ﴾ [النساء : ١٦٤] واختلف في الملكين الكاتبين هل يتبدلان بالليل والنهار، فقيل يتبدلان للحديث الصحيح يتعاقبون فيكم ملائكة بالليل وملائكة بالنهار»(۱) بناء على أنهم الحفظة وهو قول الجمهور كما نقله القاضي عياض لكن ذكر القرطبي في شرح مسلم أن الأظهر أنهم غيرهم وقيل : لا يتغيران عليه ما دام حياً. واختلف في محل جلوسهما فقيل في الفم وأن اللسان قلمهما والريق مدادهما للحديث «نقوا أفواهكم بالخلال فإنها مجلس الملكين الحافظين إلى آخره وقيل : تحت الشعر على الحنك، وقيل اليمين واليسار ثم قالوا : إن كاتب السيئات يفارقه عند الغائط والجماع . زاد القرطبي وفي الصلاة لأنه لا
قوله : (ثم قالوا إن كاتب السيئات يفارقه الخ قال ابن أمير حاج قد قيل إن الملائكة يتجنبون الإنسان عند غائطه وعند جماعة قلت : ويحتاج الجزم بهذا إلى وجود سمعي ثابت يفيده ولو ثبت ما ذكره الفقيه أبو الليث أنه روي عن أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله عنه أنه كان إذا أراد الدخول في الخلاء يبسط رداءه ويقول : أيها الملكان الحافظان علي اجلسا ههنا فإني قد عاهدت الله تعالى أن لا أتكلم في الخلاء اهـ. لكان فيه رد لهذا لكن شيخنا الحافظ أنه ضعيف .اهـ. كلامه وممن صرح : بأن المفارق في هذه الحالة الملكان معاً اللقاني في شرحه الكبير على الجوهرة وزاد أنهما يكتبان ما حصل منه بعد فراغه بعلامة يجعلها الله تعالى لهما، ولكنه لم يستند في ذلك إلى دليل فليراجع ما دليل المفارقة ومن أين أخذ صاحب البحر تخصيصها بكاتب السيئات، كذا في حواشي الدر المختار للمداري . قوله : (زاد القرطبي في الصلاة الخ يؤيده قوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم إذا قام أحدكم إلى الصلاة فلا يبصق الله ما دام في مصلاه ولا عن يمينه فإن عن يمينه ملكاً وليبصق عن يساره(٢) كذا ذكره القرطبي . قال ابن أمير حاج والحديث بهذا اللفظ في صحيح البخاري وفي دلالته على المطلوب نظر، بل الأشبه أن المراد بالملك الذي عن يمينه قرينه من الملائكة المشار إليه في صحيح مسلم بقوله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ما منكم من أحد إلا وقد وكل به قرينه من الجن وقرينه من الملائكة، قالوا: وإياك يا رسول الله؟ قال : وإياي (۳) الحديث ويؤيده ما روى الطبراني في الكبير عن أبي أمامة «إذا قام أحدكم في مصلاه فإنما يقوم بين يدي الله تعالى مستقبل ربه وملكه عن يمينه وقرينه عن يساره، والبزاق عن
يساره إنما يقع على الشيطان ولم يزد النووي في شرح مسلم على أنه إنما نهي عن البزاق عن اليمين تشريفاً لها اهـ . وأما أنه ليس في الصلاة ما يكتبه ملك السيئات ففيه نظر أيضاً لأنه قد يقع منه فيها ما يكون سيئة على أنه إن كانت العلة لملازمة الملك له تلبسه بما هو مظنة لوجود ما يكتبه والمفارقته تلبسه بما هو مظنة لعدم ذلك ينبغي أيضاً أن يكون ملك السيئات مفارقاً له في حال تلاوة القرآن والذكر ونحوه، وأن يكون الملكان مفارقين له في حالة النوم ونحوه وهو بعيد فليتأمل. اهـ. كلامه كذا في حواشي الدر المختار للمداري .
Book of Prayer - Chapter on the Description of Prayer. And twenty thousand, and the messengers are three hundred and thirteen—a great multitude. As in al-Kashshaf in Surah al-Hajj. But since it is speculative (zanni) because it is a solitary report, it does not oppose His statement: 'And messengers We have told you of before and messengers We have not told you of' [Nisa 4:164]. And they differed regarding the two recording angels (al-malakan al-katiban): do they change at night and day? It was said they change due to the authentic hadith 'Angels of the night and angels of the day alternate among you'—based on them being the guardian angels, and this is the view of the majority as reported by Qadi Iyad; but al-Qurtubi mentioned in his commentary on Muslim that the more apparent view is that they are other than the guardians. And it was said: they do not change as long as he remains alive. And they differed regarding their seating place: it was said (they sit) in the mouth, and the tongue is their pen and saliva is their ink, due to the hadith 'Clean your mouths with toothpicks, for it is the seat of the two guardian angels' etc. And it was said: under the hair on the palate, and it was said: on the right and left. Then they said: The angel of sins leaves him during defecation and intercourse. Al-Qurtubi added: and in prayer, because... Commentary: Then they said: The angel of sins leaves him, etc. Ibn Amir Haj said: It has been said that the angels avoid a person during his defecation and during intercourse. I said: Certainty about this requires an authentic transmitted source that proves it. If the report mentioned by Faqih Abu al-Layth were established—that it is narrated from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him, that when he wanted to enter the toilet he would spread his cloak and say: 'You two guardian angels, sit here, for I have made a covenant with Allah that I will not speak in the toilet'—then it would refute this. But our teacher the memorizer of hadith considered it weak. Among those who stated that both angels leave in this situation is al-Laqani in his major commentary on al-Jawhara, and he added that they write what happens from him after his completion by a sign that Allah makes for them. But he did not base that on evidence, so look into what evidence is there for departure and from where did the author of al-Bahr derive the specification that only the angel of sins leaves. As in the footnotes of al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Madari. Commentary: (Al-Qurtubi added: in prayer, etc.) It is supported by his saying, peace be upon him: 'When one of you stands for prayer, let him not spit in front of him as long as he is in his prayer place, nor to his right, for on his right is an angel; let him spit to his left' (2). Thus al-Qurtubi mentioned it. Ibn Amir Haj said: The hadith with this wording is in Sahih al-Bukhari, and there is consideration in its indication of what is intended. Rather, the more similar is that the angel on his right refers to his companion among the angels, as indicated in Sahih Muslim by his saying, peace be upon him: 'There is not one of you except that a companion from the jinn and a companion from the angels have been appointed for him.' They said: Even you, O Messenger of Allah? He said: Even me (3). This is supported by what al-Tabarani narrated in al-Kabir from Abu Umama: 'When one of you stands in his prayer place, he is standing between the hands of Allah, facing his Lord, with his angel on his right and his companion on his left, and spitting on the left only falls on the devil.' And al-Nawawi did not add in his commentary on Muslim anything except that he was prohibited from spitting on the right to honor it. As for the statement that there is nothing in prayer that the angel of sins records, there is consideration because something that is a sin may occur from him therein. And if the reason for the angel's constant attendance is his involvement in what is a locus for the existence of what he records, and his departure is due to his involvement in what is a locus for the absence of that, then it should also be that the angel of sins leaves him during recitation of Quran and remembrance and the like, and that both angels leave him during sleep and the like. This is far-fetched, so let it be considered. End of his words. As in the footnotes of al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Madari.
Source pages p. 584

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion from the sharh concerning the two recording angels (kiraman katibin). The author begins by noting that the number of angels is twenty thousand and the number of prophets is three hundred thirteen, but this is based on a solitary hadith and does not contradict the Quran. The main issue is whether the two angels who record deeds change at night and day or not. Some say they change, based on a hadith about angels alternating, identifying them as the guardian angels. Others say they do not change. The discussion then moves to their seating place: some say in the mouth (with the tongue as pen and saliva as ink), others under the hair on the palate, and others on the right and left. A key point of dispute is whether the angel who records sins leaves during defecation and intercourse. Al-Qurtubi adds that they also leave during prayer. The text then presents various opinions and testimonies, including a narration from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq who would ask the angels to stay outside the toilet, and a hadith about spitting in prayer. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes the weakness of some proofs and concludes that the matter requires further reflection. The overall tone is exploratory, not definitive.

Key Terms
الملكان الكاتبين (al-malakan al-katiban): The two angels appointed to record a person's good and bad deeds.
الحفظة (al-hafazah): The guardian angels who protect a person and record deeds; here synonymous with the two recording angels.
القرين (al-qarin): The companion angel assigned to every person, distinct from the recording angels.
كاتب السيئات (katib al-sayyiat): The angel specifically recording bad deeds, one of the two kiraman katibin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the main reason the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq questions the claim that the angel of sins leaves during prayer?
A) Because the hadith about spitting does not mention the recording angel
B) Because there is no sin committed during prayer
C) Because the Quran states that angels are always present
D) Because sleep is a more likely time for departure

Key Takeaway
The departure of the recording angels is a matter of ikhtilaf; the Hanafi school holds that the angels are always present, as the evidence for departure is weak.

Imam's Actions After Salam
Ruling on imam's post-salam actions with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam's actions after salam for both cases (with and without nafl) and identify the evidence from the hadith of al-Bara'.

Core Idea
Imam's turning after salam is sunnah; sitting facing congregation without reason is bid'ah.

The author of Kanz al-Daqaiq did not specify what the imam should do after the salam. In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the commentator explains that the imam's action depends on whether he intends to pray a voluntary prayer (nafl) after the obligatory one. The ruling is derived from the practice of the Companions, who preferred to be on the Prophet's right so he would turn towards them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Determine whether the imam intends to pray a voluntary prayer (nafl) after the obligatory prayer or not.
The ruling changes based on this intention.
2
State the ruling for each scenario
If intending nafl, he should stand and move from his place to the right or left. If not intending nafl, he may sit in his place or turn as he wishes.
Sitting facing the congregation in the first scenario is considered an innovation (bid'ah).
3
Identify the preferred view (mufta bihi)
The relied-upon position from al-Khaniyya and al-Muhit is that it is mustahabb to turn to the right of the qibla.
This is supported by the hadith of al-Bara'.
4
Analyze the hadith evidence
In Sahih Muslim, the Companions said they loved to be on the right of the Prophet so he would turn his face towards them. This indicates the desirability of the imam turning.
The hadith shows preference, not obligation (zanni dalala).
5
Understand the hukm level
The imam's movement after salam is sunnah (mustahabb), not wajib. It is not a fard or rukn of the prayer.
The authority comes from later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف ما يفعله بعد السلام وقد قالوا : إن كان إماماً وكانت صلاة يتنفل بعدها فإنه يقوم ويتحول عن مكانه إما يمنة أو يسرة وخلفه والجلوس مستقبلاً بدعة وإن كان لا يتنفل بعدها يقعد مكانه وإن شاء انحرف يميناً أو شمالاً، وإن شاء استقبلهم بوجهه إلا أن يكون بحذائه مصل، سواء كان في الصف الأول أو في الأخير والاستقبال إلى المصلي مكروه هذا ما صححه في البدائع، واختار في الخانية والمحيط استحباب أن ينحرف عن يمين القبلة وأن يصلي فيها ويمين القبلة ما بحذاء يسار المستقبل ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم من حديث البراء كنا إذا صلينا خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أحببنا أن نكون عن يمينه يقبل علينا بوجهه .
And the author did not mention what he does after the salam. And they said: If he is an imam and it is a prayer after which he intends to pray a voluntary prayer, then he should stand and move from his place either to the right or left and behind him, and sitting facing (the congregation) is an innovation. And if he does not intend to pray a voluntary prayer after it, he sits in his place; and if he wishes, he turns right or left, and if he wishes, he faces them with his face, unless there is a worshipper directly in line with him, whether in the first row or the last. Facing the worshipper is disliked. This is what was authenticated in al-Bada'i'. And in al-Khaniyya and al-Muhit, it is chosen as recommended that he turn to the right of the qibla and pray there; and the right of the qibla is what is opposite the left of the person facing it. And that is supported by what is in Sahih Muslim from the hadith of al-Bara': We used to, when we prayed behind the Prophet, peace be upon him, we loved to be on his right so that he would turn his face towards us.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a ruling regarding what the imam should do after completing the obligatory prayer. The text presents two scenarios: if the imam intends to pray a voluntary prayer (nafl) after the obligatory one, he should stand and move from his place to the right or left, and sitting down facing the congregation is considered an innovation (bidah). If he does not intend to pray nafl, he may sit in his place or turn to face the congregation, unless there is a worshipper directly in front of him; in that case, facing the worshipper is makruh. The preferred view (in al-Khaniyya and al-Muhit) is that the imam should turn to the right of the qibla and pray there. The proof is a hadith from al-Bara' indicating that the Companions preferred to be on the right of the Prophet so he would turn to them. This ruling is specific to the imam, and the Hanafi position is clarified: the imam's turning is recommended, not obligatory.

Key Terms
بدعة (bid'ah): An innovation in religion, here referring to sitting facing the congregation after salam without a valid reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should the imam do if he does not intend to pray a voluntary prayer after the obligatory one?
A) He must stand and move to the right
B) He may sit in his place or turn as he wishes
C) He must leave the mosque immediately
D) He must recite additional dhikr

Key Takeaway
The imam's action after salam depends on whether he intends nafl: moving is recommended, sitting facing the congregation without nafl is permissible but innovation if done as regular practice.

Jahr and Ikhfa in Prayer: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with Quranic proof and commentary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for loud and silent recitation in obligatory and voluntary prayers and explain the Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
The imam recites loudly in Fajr, first two rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha, Friday, and Eid; silently in all other prayers.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on when to recite loudly (jahr) and silently (ikhfa) during prayer. The ruling is based on the Prophet's practice and a Quranic verse commanding moderation. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the basis and addresses a nuance about voluntary night prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayers requiring jahr
Look at the matn: 'وجهر بقراءة الفجر وأولي العشاءين ولو قضاء والجمعة والعيدين'. These are Fajr, first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha (even if makeup), Friday, and both Eid prayers.
'العشاءين' refers to Maghrib and Isha.
2
Identify the prayers requiring ikhfa
The text says 'ويسر في غيرها' meaning silently in all other prayers, such as Zuhr and Asr, and the later rak'ahs of Maghrib/Isha.
This includes the third of Maghrib and third/fourth of Isha for the imam.
3
Note the exception for the one praying alone
The matn indicates that a person praying alone has a choice between jahr and ikhfa, similar to a voluntary prayer at night. The commentator discusses this point.
The sharh criticizes the author's lack of restriction for voluntary night prayer.
4
Examine the Quranic proof
The passage cites Quran 17:110: 'ولا تجهر بصلاتك ولا تخافت بها وابتغ بين ذلك سبيلا'. This was revealed when the Prophet's loud recitation caused harm from polytheists.
The verse commands moderation, but the Sunnah specifies when each is to be used.
5
Understand the sabab al-nuzul and its application
Initially the Prophet recited loudly in all prayers. The polytheists insulted him and the Quran. Allah revealed the verse to instruct him to moderate, leading to the distinct rules for jahr and ikhfa.
This shows that the ruling is derived from both Quran and Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وجهر بقراءة الفجر وأولي العشاءين ولو قضاء والجمعة والعيدين ويسر في غيرها كمتنفل بالنهار وخير المنفرد فيما يجهر كمتنفل بالليل شروع في بيان القراءة وصفتها، وقدم صفتها من الجهر والإخفاء لأنه : يعم المفروض وغيره، والأصل فيه كما ذكره المصنف في الكافي أن النبي الله كان يجهر بالقرآن في الصلوات كلها في الابتداء وكان المشركون يؤذونه ويسبون من أنزل وأنزل عليه فأنزل الله تعالى ولا تجهر بصلاتك ولا تخافت بها [الإسراء: ۱۱۰] أي لا تجهر بصلاتك كلها ولا تخافت بها كلها وابتغ بين ذلك سبيلاً بأن
قوله : (والمتنفل بالليل مخير بين الجهر والإخفاء إن كان منفرداً الخ) قال في النهر بعد تقييد كلام المصنف بذلك : ولم أر من عرج على هذا من شراح هذا الكتاب، واعتذر عن المصنف بأنه استغنى عن التقييد لكون الكلام فيه اهـ. وهذا عجيب إذ هو مذكور هنا تبعاً للشارح، هذا
His saying: (And he recites loudly in the recitation of Fajr and the first two of the two evening prayers (Maghrib and Isha), even if make-up, and Friday and the two Eids, and he recites silently in other than them, like a voluntary prayer during the day; and the one praying alone has a choice regarding what is recited loudly, like a voluntary prayer at night.) This is the beginning of explaining the recitation and its description. He presented its description of loudness and softness because it includes obligatory and other. The basis for it, as the author mentioned in al-Kafi, is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to recite the Quran loudly in all prayers initially, but the polytheists would harm him and insult the one who revealed and what was revealed to him. So Allah revealed: 'And do not recite loudly in your prayer, nor silently in it' (al-Isra 17:110), meaning do not recite loudly in all your prayer nor silently in all of it, but seek a way between that, by... His saying: (And the one praying voluntarily at night is given a choice between loudness and softness if he is alone, etc.) He said in al-Nahr after restricting the author's statement by that: 'I have not seen anyone who commented on this from the commentators of this book, and he made an excuse for the author that he dispensed with the restriction because the discussion is about it.' This is strange, for it is mentioned here following the commentator.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling about loud (jahr) and silent (ikhfa) recitation in prayer. The matn states that the imam recites loudly in Fajr, the first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha (the two evening prayers), even if making up a missed prayer, and also in Friday and Eid prayers. He recites silently in all other prayers, similar to a voluntary prayer during the day. A person praying alone has a choice regarding loud recitation, like a voluntary prayer at night. The sharh explains that the author first discusses the quality of recitation (loud/soft) because it applies to both obligatory and supererogatory prayers. The basis is that the Prophet initially recited loudly in all prayers until the polytheists harmed him, then Allah revealed the verse from Surah al-Isra instructing moderation. The commentary then addresses a point about the voluntary prayer at night: the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq notes that he did not see any other commentator discussing this and considers it strange that the author did not restrict the ruling, but excuses him. This passage clarifies the Hanafi position on jahr and ikhfa.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation of Quran in prayer such that others can hear.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa): Silent recitation where only the person himself can hear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, in which of the following prayers does the imam recite silently (ikhfa)?
A) Fajr
B) Zuhr
C) Maghrib (first two rak'ahs)
D) Eid prayer

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite loudly in Fajr, first two rak'ahs of Maghrib and Isha, Friday, and Eid; silently in all other prayers; a person alone has a choice.

Imam's Actions After Salam and Their Proof
Ruling with proof on imam's post-salam actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) action for an imam after completing the fard prayer and apply the condition that it is not obligatory.

Core Idea
An imam should move to a different spot after salam if praying sunnah; facing a person in prayer is makruh.

The great Hanafi jurists discussed what an imam should do after concluding the obligatory prayer. Should he remain seated, turn to face the congregation, or move to another place? This lesson unpacks the recommended practice, the intra-madhhab differences, and the prophetic proof that settles the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The imam after salam either intends to pray the sunnah prayer or does not. The ruling differs for each.
Scenarios: (a) he will pray sunnah, (b) he will not.
2
Determine the ruling for each scenario
If he intends sunnah, he should stand and move to another spot (right or left). If not, he may stay or turn, but facing a person in prayer is disliked.
Sunnah ghayr muakkadah for moving; permissible (mubah) to stay/turn.
3
Note the exception
Even if not praying sunnah, if there is a person praying directly in front, he must not face them. Facing a mausoleum? Not discussed.
Makruh tahrimi? The text says makruh, likely tanzihi.
4
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of al-Bara' ibn 'Azib in Sahih Muslim: the Companions loved to be on the right of the Prophet so that he would face them with his face.
الحديث: كنا إذا صلينا خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أحببنا أن نكون عن يمينه يقبل علينا بوجهه
5
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of turning to face them indicates recommendation, not obligation. If it were obligatory, he would have commanded it; instead, he simply did it.
The Hanafi principle: al-amr (command) indicates obligation, but here it is just fi'l (action), which indicates istihbab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة الأيمن أو الأيسر أو فيهما لو محاذياً وجهر بقراءة الفجر وأولي العشاءين ولو قضاء والجمعة والعيدين ويسر في غيرها كمتنفل بالنهار وخير المنفرد فيما يجهر كمتنفل بالليل يفعل سيئة فيها . ثم اختلفوا فيما يكتبانه فقيل ما فيه أجر أو وزر، وعزاه في الاختيار إلى محمد، وقيل يكتبان كل شيء حتى أنينه في مرضه. ثم اختلفوا متى يمحى المباح فقيل آخر النهار، وقيل يوم الخميس، والأكثرون على أنها تمحى يوم القيامة. كذا في الاختيار. وذكر بعض المفسرين أنه الصحيح عند المحققين والمختار أن كيفية الكتابة والمكتوب فيه مما لا يعلمها إلا الله تعالى وقد أوسع الكلام في هذا العلامة ابن أمير حاج في شرح منية المصلي وذكر أن الصبي المميز لا ينوي الكتبة إذ ليسوا معه وإنما ينوي الحافظين له من الشياطين، ولذا لم يقل المصنف والكتبة ليعم كل مصل. ولم يذكر المصنف ما يفعله بعد السلام وقد قالوا : إن كان إماماً وكانت صلاة يتنفل بعدها فإنه يقوم ويتحول عن مكانه إما يمنة أو يسرة وخلفه والجلوس مستقبلاً ،بدعة وإن كان لا يتنفل بعدها يقعد مكانه وإن شاء انحرف يميناً أو شمالاً، وإن شاء استقبلهم بوجهه إلا أن يكون بحذائه مصل، سواء كان في الصف الأول أو في الأخير والاستقبال إلى المصلي مكروه هذا ما صححه في البدائع، واختار في الخانية والمحيط استحباب أن ينحرف عن يمين القبلة وأن يصلي فيها ويمين القبلة ما بحذاء يسار المستقبل ويشهد له ما في صحيح مسلم من حديث البراء كنا إذا صلينا خلف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أحببنا أن نكون عن يمينه يقبل علينا بوجهه .
Book of Prayer - Section on Description of Prayer. The right or the left or both if aligned, and he recites aloud in Fajr and the first two of the two evening prayers even if qada, and in Jumu'a and the two Eids, and he recites silently in others, like one who prays supererogatory by day, and the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited aloud, like one who prays supererogatory by night; he commits a sin therein. Then they differed over what they write: some said only what has reward or sin, attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani; others said they write everything, even his moaning in illness. Then they differed when permissible things are erased: some said at the end of the day, others on Thursday, but most say they are erased on the Day of Judgment. This is in al-Ikhtiyar. Some commentators said that the correct view among verifiers is that the manner of writing and what is written are known only to Allah. The scholar Ibn Amir Hajj has expanded on this in his commentary on Munyat al-Musalli. He mentioned that the discerning child does not intend the recording, as they are not with him; rather he intends the guardians for him from devils. Therefore the author did not say 'and the recording' to include every worshipper. The author did not mention what one does after the salam. They said: If he is an imam and the prayer is one after which supererogatory prayer is made, he stands and moves from his place either to the right or left and behind him, and sitting facing the people is an innovation. If he does not pray supererogatory after it, he stays in his place, or if he wishes, he turns right or left, or if he wishes, he faces them with his face, unless there is a praying person in line with him, whether in the first row or the last. Facing the one praying is disliked. This is what is considered correct in al-Bada'i'. In al-Khaniyah and al-Muhit they chose the recommendation of turning to the right of the qibla and praying there, and the right of the qibla is what is alongside the left of the one facing it. This is supported by what is in Sahih Muslim from the hadith of al-Bara: 'When we prayed behind the Prophet , we loved to be on his right so that he would face us with his face.'
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a sharh (commentary) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It opens by discussing the rulings related to the two recording angels (kiraman katibin). The text reports ikhtilaf on what they record: the stronger view (attributed to Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that they record only acts with reward or punishment; another view says everything including permissible moans. The erasure of permissible deeds is also disputed: most say they are erased only on Judgment Day. The commentator then notes that the true nature of this recording is known only to Allah. He then addresses the case of a discerning child (sabi mumayyiz): the child does not intend the angels' recording but rather seeks protection from devils. The main ruling begins after salam. For the imam: if he intends to pray the sunnah after fard, it is sunnah for him to stand and move to another spot (right or left) to perform it. If he does not pray sunnah, he may stay or turn. However, it is makruh (disliked) to face a person who is still praying, even if in the same row. The relied-upon position (sahhaha in al-Bada'i') is that he should turn away. Some later works (al-Khaniyah, al-Muhit) recommend turning to the right of the qibla, supported by the hadith of al-Bara' from Sahih Muslim. The passage thus provides both the ruling and its prophetic proof.

Key Terms
الصبي المميز (al-sabi al-mumayyiz): A child who has reached the age of discernment (about 7 years) and can differentiate between right and wrong.
الكتبة (al-kitabah): The act of the recording angels (kiraman katibin) writing down deeds.
استحباب (istihbab): Recommendation; an action that is encouraged but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should an imam do after completing the fard prayer if he intends to pray the sunnah prayer?
A) He must remain seated and not move.
B) He should get up and move to a different spot, preferably to the right.
C) He should turn to face the congregation while remaining seated.
D) He should leave the mosque.

Key Takeaway
An imam should move to a different spot after salam if he intends to pray sunnah; facing a person in prayer is makruh.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
The Imam's Obligation of Loud and Silent Recitation
Ruling with proof on imam's jahr and ikhfa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five prayers where the imam must recite loudly and identify the Quranic proof for this ruling.

Core Idea
The imam must recite loudly in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha (first two), Jumu'a, and Eids; silently in others.

This lesson establishes the ruling of jahr (loud) and ikhfa (silent) recitation for the imam in congregational prayers. The ruling is based on the Quranic verse (al-Isra 17:110) and the perpetual practice of the Prophet ﷺ, which has been preserved through consensus. We will examine the specific prayers and the proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act? Recitation in prayer. What is the ruling? Loud or silent depending on the prayer.
The ruling is wajib for the imam.
2
Locate the dalil
Quran 17:110 and the Prophet's practice after revelation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse commands moderation; the Prophet's actual practice defined which prayers are loud and which silent.
4
List the five loud prayers
Fajr, first two of Maghrib and Isha, Jumu'a, and the two Eids.
Even if qada, the ruling applies.
5
Note the consensus and exception
Consensus (ijma) on these; the imam has no choice; the ruling is obligatory.
Supererogatory prayers by day: silent; by night: choice for munfarid (covered in next lesson).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وجهر بقراءة الفجر وأولي العشاءين ولو قضاء والجمعة والعيدين ويسر في غيرها كمتنفل بالنهار وخير المنفرد فيما يجهر كمتنفل بالليل شروع في بيان القراءة وصفتها، وقدم صفتها من الجهر والإخفاء لأنه : يعم المفروض وغيره، والأصل فيه كما ذكره المصنف في الكافي أن النبي الله كان يجهر بالقرآن في الصلوات كلها في الابتداء وكان المشركون يؤذونه ويسبون من أنزل وأنزل عليه فأنزل الله تعالى ولا تجهر بصلاتك ولا تخافت بها [الإسراء: ۱۱۰] أي لا تجهر بصلاتك كلها ولا تخافت بها كلها وابتغ بين ذلك سبيلاً بأن يساره إنما يقع على الشيطان ولم يزد النووي في شرح مسلم على أنه إنما نهي عن البزاق عن اليمين تشريفاً لها اهـ . وأما أنه ليس في الصلاة ما يكتبه ملك السيئات ففيه نظر أيضاً لأنه قد يقع منه فيها ما يكون سيئة على أنه إن كانت العلة لملازمة الملك له تلبسه بما هو . مظنة لوجود ما يكتبه والمفارقته تلبسه بما هو مظنة لعدم ذلك ينبغي أيضاً أن يكون ملك السيئات مفارقاً له في حال تلاوة القرآن والذكر ونحوه، وأن يكون الملكان مفارقين له في حالة النوم ونحوه وهو بعيد فليتأمل. اهـ. كلامه كذا في حواشي الدر المختار للمداري . قوله : (والمتنفل بالليل مخير بين الجهر والإخفاء إن كان منفرداً الخ) قال في النهر بعد تقييد كلام المصنف بذلك : ولم أر من عرج على هذا من شراح هذا الكتاب، واعتذر عن المصنف بأنه استغنى عن التقييد لكون الكلام فيه اهـ. وهذا عجيب إذ هو مذكور هنا تبعاً للشارح، هذا وفي تجهر بصلاة الليل وتخافت بصلاة النهار فكان يخافت بعد ذلك في صلاة الظهر والعصر لأنهم كانوا مستعدين للإيذاء في هذين الوقتين ويجهر في المغرب لأنهم كانوا مشغولين بالأكل، العشاء والفجر لكونهم رقوداً. وفي الجمعة والعيدين لأنه أقامهما بالمدينة وما كان للكفار بها قوة. وهذا العذر وإن زال بغلبة المسلمين فالحكم باق لأن بقاءه يستغني عن بقاء السبب ولأنه أخلف عذراً آخر وهو كثرة اشتغال الناس في هاتين الصلاتين دون غيرهما اهـ. وقد انعقد الإجماع على الجهر فيما ذكر وقد قدمنا أن الجهر في هذه المواضع واجب على الإمام للمواظبة من النبي . وتخصيصه بالإمام مفهوم من قوله هنا وخير المنفرد فيما يجهر» فأفاد أن الإمام ليس بمخير قالوا ولا يجهد الإمام نفسه بالجهر. وفي السراج الوهاج : الإمام إذا جهر فوق حاجة الناس فقد أسار وأفاد أنه لا فرق في حق الإمام بين الأداء والقضاء لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. والحق بالجمعة والعيدين التراويح والوتر في رمضان للتوارث المنقول، والمراد بغيرهما الثالثة من المغرب والأخريان العشاء وجميع ركعات الظهر والعصر. وقد أفاد أن المتنفل بالنهار يجب عليه الإخفاء مطلقاً والمتنفل بالليل مخير بين الجهر والإخفاء إن كان منفرداً، أما إن كان إماماً فالجهر واجب كما ذكره الشارح رحمه الله، وأن المنفرد ليس بمخير في الصلاة السرية بل يجب الإخفاء عليه وهو الصحيح لأن الإمام يجب عليه الإخفاء فالمنفرد أولى. وذكر عصام بن يوسف أن المنفرد مخير فيما يخافت فيه أيضاً استدلالاً بعدم وجوب سجود السهو عليه، وتعقبه الشارح بأن الإمام إنما وجب عليه سجود السهو لأن جنايته أعظم لأنه ارتكب الجهر والإسماع بخلاف المنفرد، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنا لا ننكر أن واجباً قد يكون أكد من واجب لكن لما لم ينط وجوب السهو إلا بترك الواجب لا بآكد الواجب ولا برتبة مخصوصة منه فحيث كانت المخافتة واجبة على المنفرد ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود. من وفي العناية : إن ظاهر الرواية أن المنفرد مخير فيما يخافت فيه أيضاً وفيه تأمل. والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب . وفي قوله فيما يجهر» دلالة على أن المنفرد مخير في الصلاة الجهرية إذا وفي السراج بعد ذكره التخيير اعتباراً بالفرض قال : والجهر أفضل وعزاه إلى المبسوط. قوله: (ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود) قال الشيخ اسمعيل أقول : وجوب سجود السهو على المنفرد إذا جهر فيما يخافت فيه رواية عن أبي حنيفة ذكرت في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي البرجندي معزياً إلى الظهيرية : وروى أبو سليمان أن المنفرد إذا ظن أنه إمام فجهر كما جهر الإمام يلزمه سجود السهو. ويلائمه ما في المحيط : إذا جهر المنفرد من صلاة المخافتة كان مسيئاً، وفي صلاة الجهر يتخير. كذا في عامة الروايات والذي جزم الحلواني بأنه ظاهر الجواب أنه لا سهو على المنفرد. وفي الخلاصة: لا على المنفرد إذا خافت فيما يجهر به وبالعكس وسيأتي مفصلاً في بابه .اهـ. قلت : ومثله في التتارخانية عن المحيط والذخيرة كما سنذكره في بابه إن شاء الله تعالى قوله : (والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب) فيه سهو
His statement: (And he recites aloud in Fajr and the first two of the two evening prayers even if qada, and Jumu'a and the two Eids, and he recites silently in others, like one who prays supererogatory by day, and the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited aloud, like one who prays supererogatory by night.) Beginning of explanation of recitation and its description. He presented its description of loudness and softness because it covers obligatory and other prayers. The basis for it, as the author mentioned in al-Kafi, is that the Prophet used to recite aloud in all prayers initially, and the polytheists harmed and insulted him and what was revealed to him, so Allah revealed: 'And do not recite loudly in your prayer nor silently, but seek a way between that' (al-Isra 17:110), meaning do not recite all of your prayer loudly nor all of it silently, but seek a way between that. ... So he used to recite silently after that in Zuhr and Asr because they were ready to harm in those times, and aloud in Maghrib because they were busy eating, and in Isha and Fajr because they were asleep. For Jumu'a and the two Eids, because he established them in Medina and the disbelievers had no power there. This excuse is gone with Muslim dominance, but the ruling remains because its continuation does not need the continuation of the cause, and because it substitutes another excuse: people's busyness in these two prayers more than others. Consensus has been reached on loudness in what was mentioned, and we have already stated that loudness in these places is wajib upon the imam due to the Prophet's continuous practice. Its specification to the imam is understood from his statement here 'and the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited aloud', which indicates that the imam has no choice. They said: The imam should not strain himself in loudness. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the imam recites louder than people's need, he has acted wrongly. It also indicates that there is no difference for the imam between performance and makeup because makeup replicates performance. Tarawih and witr in Ramadan are joined to Jumu'a and the two Eids by transmitted custom. What is meant by 'other than them' is the third rak'ah of Maghrib, the last two of Isha, and all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr. It is also established that the one who prays supererogatory by day must recite silently absolutely, and the one who prays supererogatory by night has a choice between loudness and silence if he is alone. But if he is an imam, loudness is wajib as mentioned by the commentator (Allah's mercy). And that the one praying alone does not have a choice in the silent prayer; rather silence is obligatory upon him, and this is the correct view because the imam must recite silently, so the individual is even more entitled. 'Isam ibn Yusuf mentioned that the individual has a choice in what one recites silently too, using as evidence the lack of obligation of sajda al-sahw upon him. The commentator refuted him: the imam's sajda al-sahw is obligatory because his violation is greater, as he committed loudness and making others hear, unlike the individual. This was further refuted in Fath al-Qadir: We do not deny that a wajib may be more emphatic than another wajib, but since sajda al-sahw is not made obligatory except by abandoning a wajib, not by a more emphatic wajib nor by a particular rank of it, where silence is wajib upon the individual, it should be that abandoning it necessitates sajda. In al-'Inayah: The apparent transmission is that the individual has a choice in what one recites silently too, but this requires reflection. The apparent view of the school is obligation. In his statement 'in what is recited aloud' there is indication that the individual has a choice in the loud prayer. In al-Siraj after mentioning the choice by analogy to obligatory prayer, he said: Loudness is better, and he attributed it to al-Mabsut. His statement: (it should be that abandoning it necessitates sajda). Shaykh Isma'il said: I say: The obligation of sajda al-sahw upon the individual if he recites aloud in what one recites silently is a narration from Abu Hanifa mentioned in al-Dhakhira etc. In al-Barjandi, attributing to al-Zuhayriyya: Abu Sulayman narrated that if the individual thinks he is an imam and recites aloud like the imam, sajda al-sahw is obligatory upon him. This is consistent with what is in al-Muhit: If the individual recites aloud in a silent prayer, he has done wrongly; in a loud prayer he has a choice. Thus in all narrations. Al-Halwani definitively stated that the apparent answer is that there is no sajda upon the individual. In al-Khulasa: There is no sajda upon the individual if he recites silently in what is recited aloud, and vice versa, and it will come in detail in its chapter. End. I say: Similarly in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira, as we will mention in its chapter if Allah wills. His statement: (And the apparent view of the school is obligation) contains an oversight.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a detailed sharh on the ruling of jahr (loud) and ikhfa (silent) recitation in prayer. It begins by quoting the matn: the imam must recite aloud in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha (first two rak'ahs), Jumu'a, and the two Eids, even in qada; and he must recite silently in Zuhr, Asr, and the third of Maghrib, etc. The commentator explains the origin from Surah al-Isra' (17:110) and the Prophet's practice: initially he recited loudly, but due to polytheist harm, the verse came, leading to distinct loud and silent prayers. The ruling remains even after the cause is gone because it is now established by Shariah. It is wajib for the imam to recite loudly in these places due to the Prophet's continuous practice; the munfarid (individual praying alone) is not obliged to be loud. The core ikhtilaf is whether the munfarid has a choice in silent prayers. The text reports 'Isam ibn Yusuf's view that the munfarid is mukhayyar, using the absence of sajda al-sahw as evidence. The commentator rejects this: the imam's violation is greater (he also makes others hear), so sajda is imposed on him; the munfarid's obligation to be silent is still wajib, and if he recites loudly, he is sinful and according to some narrations (e.g., from Abu Hanifa in al-Dhakhira) he must perform sajda al-sahw. However, other authorities like al-Halwani hold that no sajda is required. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers (wajib), and that loudness in these is makruh and may necessitate sajda. For voluntary prayers by day, silence is wajib; by night, the munfarid may choose, but loudness is better. The passage also notes that tarawih and witr in Ramadan are treated like Jumu'a and Eid in terms of loudness.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Reciting the Quran aloud in prayer, audible to others.
إخفاء (ikhfā'): Reciting silently, moving the lips without sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following prayers must the imam recite loudly according to the Hanafi school?
A) Zuhr and Asr
B) Fajr and Jumu'a
C) Maghrib (all three rak'ahs)
D) Isha (all four rak'ahs)

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite loudly in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha (first two), Jumu'a, and Eids; this is wajib based on Quran and consensus.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Munfarid's Recitation: Choice or Obligation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on munfarid's recitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on the munfarid's recitation in silent prayers and evaluate the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
The munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers, though some Hanafi authorities said he has a choice.

This lesson addresses the ruling for a person praying alone (munfarid) regarding loud and silent recitation. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the munfarid must be silent in silent prayers, just like the imam; other narrations give him a choice. We will examine the proofs and the role of sajda al-sahw in settling the dispute.

Guided Path
1
State the mufta bihi position
The munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers; in loud prayers he may choose but jahr is better.
2
Identify the opposing view
'Isam ibn Yusuf and the apparent transmission in al-'Inayah hold that the munfarid has choice in silent prayers.
They use absence of sajda as evidence.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
Opponents argue that since no sajda al-sahw is required, it is not wajib.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The imam's sajda is due to greater violation; the munfarid's wajib is still there, and some narrations require sajda.
Abu Hanifa's narration in al-Dhakhira requires sajda.
5
Determine the tarjih
The commentator prefers wujub; the majority of later scholars adopt this.
The passage states: 'والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب' (the apparent view of the school is obligation).

لأن جنايته أعظم لأنه ارتكب الجهر والإسماع بخلاف المنفرد، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنا لا ننكر أن واجباً قد يكون أكد من واجب لكن لما لم ينط وجوب السهو إلا بترك الواجب لا بآكد الواجب ولا برتبة مخصوصة منه فحيث كانت المخافتة واجبة على المنفرد ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود. من وفي العناية : إن ظاهر الرواية أن المنفرد مخير فيما يخافت فيه أيضاً وفيه تأمل. والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب . وفي قوله فيما يجهر» دلالة على أن المنفرد مخير في الصلاة الجهرية إذا وفي السراج بعد ذكره التخيير اعتباراً بالفرض قال : والجهر أفضل وعزاه إلى المبسوط. قوله: (ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود) قال الشيخ اسمعيل أقول : وجوب سجود السهو على المنفرد إذا جهر فيما يخافت فيه رواية عن أبي حنيفة ذكرت في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي البرجندي معزياً إلى الظهيرية : وروى أبو سليمان أن المنفرد إذا ظن أنه إمام فجهر كما جهر الإمام يلزمه سجود السهو. ويلائمه ما في المحيط : إذا جهر المنفرد من صلاة المخافتة كان مسيئاً، وفي صلاة الجهر يتخير. كذا في عامة الروايات والذي جزم الحلواني بأنه ظاهر الجواب أنه لا سهو على المنفرد. وفي الخلاصة: لا على المنفرد إذا خافت فيما يجهر به وبالعكس وسيأتي مفصلاً في بابه .اهـ. قلت : ومثله في التتارخانية عن المحيط والذخيرة كما سنذكره في بابه إن شاء الله تعالى قوله : (والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب) فيه سهو
His statement: (And he recites aloud in Fajr and the first two of the two evening prayers even if qada, and Jumu'a and the two Eids, and he recites silently in others, like one who prays supererogatory by day, and the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited aloud, like one who prays supererogatory by night.) Beginning of explanation of recitation and its description. He presented its description of loudness and softness because it covers obligatory and other prayers. The basis for it, as the author mentioned in al-Kafi, is that the Prophet used to recite aloud in all prayers initially, and the polytheists harmed and insulted him and what was revealed to him, so Allah revealed: 'And do not recite loudly in your prayer nor silently, but seek a way between that' (al-Isra 17:110), meaning do not recite all of your prayer loudly nor all of it silently, but seek a way between that. ... So he used to recite silently after that in Zuhr and Asr because they were ready to harm in those times, and aloud in Maghrib because they were busy eating, and in Isha and Fajr because they were asleep. For Jumu'a and the two Eids, because he established them in Medina and the disbelievers had no power there. This excuse is gone with Muslim dominance, but the ruling remains because its continuation does not need the continuation of the cause, and because it substitutes another excuse: people's busyness in these two prayers more than others. Consensus has been reached on loudness in what was mentioned, and we have already stated that loudness in these places is wajib upon the imam due to the Prophet's continuous practice. Its specification to the imam is understood from his statement here 'and the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited aloud', which indicates that the imam has no choice. They said: The imam should not strain himself in loudness. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If the imam recites louder than people's need, he has acted wrongly. It also indicates that there is no difference for the imam between performance and makeup because makeup replicates performance. Tarawih and witr in Ramadan are joined to Jumu'a and the two Eids by transmitted custom. What is meant by 'other than them' is the third rak'ah of Maghrib, the last two of Isha, and all rak'ahs of Zuhr and Asr. It is also established that the one who prays supererogatory by day must recite silently absolutely, and the one who prays supererogatory by night has a choice between loudness and silence if he is alone. But if he is an imam, loudness is wajib as mentioned by the commentator (Allah's mercy). And that the one praying alone does not have a choice in the silent prayer; rather silence is obligatory upon him, and this is the correct view because the imam must recite silently, so the individual is even more entitled. 'Isam ibn Yusuf mentioned that the individual has a choice in what one recites silently too, using as evidence the lack of obligation of sajda al-sahw upon him. The commentator refuted him: the imam's sajda al-sahw is obligatory because his violation is greater, as he committed loudness and making others hear, unlike the individual. This was further refuted in Fath al-Qadir: We do not deny that a wajib may be more emphatic than another wajib, but since sajda al-sahw is not made obligatory except by abandoning a wajib, not by a more emphatic wajib nor by a particular rank of it, where silence is wajib upon the individual, it should be that abandoning it necessitates sajda. In al-'Inayah: The apparent transmission is that the individual has a choice in what one recites silently too, but this requires reflection. The apparent view of the school is obligation. In his statement 'in what is recited aloud' there is indication that the individual has a choice in the loud prayer. In al-Siraj after mentioning the choice by analogy to obligatory prayer, he said: Loudness is better, and he attributed it to al-Mabsut. His statement: (it should be that abandoning it necessitates sajda). Shaykh Isma'il said: I say: The obligation of sajda al-sahw upon the individual if he recites aloud in what one recites silently is a narration from Abu Hanifa mentioned in al-Dhakhira etc. In al-Barjandi, attributing to al-Zuhayriyya: Abu Sulayman narrated that if the individual thinks he is an imam and recites aloud like the imam, sajda al-sahw is obligatory upon him. This is consistent with what is in al-Muhit: If the individual recites aloud in a silent prayer, he has done wrongly; in a loud prayer he has a choice. Thus in all narrations. Al-Halwani definitively stated that the apparent answer is that there is no sajda upon the individual. In al-Khulasa: There is no sajda upon the individual if he recites silently in what is recited aloud, and vice versa, and it will come in detail in its chapter. End. I say: Similarly in al-Tatarakhaniyya from al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira, as we will mention in its chapter if Allah wills. His statement: (And the apparent view of the school is obligation) contains an oversight.
Source pages p. 585

Commentary
This passage is a detailed sharh on the ruling of jahr (loud) and ikhfa (silent) recitation in prayer. It begins by quoting the matn: the imam must recite aloud in Fajr, Maghrib, Isha (first two rak'ahs), Jumu'a, and the two Eids, even in qada; and he must recite silently in Zuhr, Asr, and the third of Maghrib, etc. The commentator explains the origin from Surah al-Isra' (17:110) and the Prophet's practice: initially he recited loudly, but due to polytheist harm, the verse came, leading to distinct loud and silent prayers. The ruling remains even after the cause is gone because it is now established by Shariah. It is wajib for the imam to recite loudly in these places due to the Prophet's continuous practice; the munfarid (individual praying alone) is not obliged to be loud. The core ikhtilaf is whether the munfarid has a choice in silent prayers. The text reports 'Isam ibn Yusuf's view that the munfarid is mukhayyar, using the absence of sajda al-sahw as evidence. The commentator rejects this: the imam's violation is greater (he also makes others hear), so sajda is imposed on him; the munfarid's obligation to be silent is still wajib, and if he recites loudly, he is sinful and according to some narrations (e.g., from Abu Hanifa in al-Dhakhira) he must perform sajda al-sahw. However, other authorities like al-Halwani hold that no sajda is required. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers (wajib), and that loudness in these is makruh and may necessitate sajda. For voluntary prayers by day, silence is wajib; by night, the munfarid may choose, but loudness is better. The passage also notes that tarawih and witr in Ramadan are treated like Jumu'a and Eid in terms of loudness.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not as an imam or in congregation.
سجود السهو (sajdat al-sahw): Prostration performed to compensate for an unintentional error in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for a person praying alone (munfarid) in a silent prayer like Zuhr?
A) He may choose to recite aloud or silently; both are permissible.
B) He must recite silently; if he recites aloud, he is sinful and may need to perform sajda al-sahw.
C) He must recite aloud because it is better.
D) He must only recite silently if he is afraid of disturbing others.

Key Takeaway
The munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers; this is the relied-upon Hanafi view despite some early authorities granting a choice.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Obligation of Jahr on the Imam in Specific Prayers
Clarifying where jahr is wajib on the imam and why

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the prayers in which jahr is wajib upon the imam, explain the reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling, and distinguish the imam's obligation from the munfarid's choice.

Core Idea
The imam must recite loudly in Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, Jumuah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi position on loud versus silent recitation in prayer. The author explains that the Prophet's constant practice established a pattern: jahr in certain prayers and ikhfa in others, based on prevailing circumstances. Even though the original reasons have changed, the ruling remains wajib due to consensus and continuity of practice. Understanding this distinction is essential for the imam who leads prayer and for the student of fiqh who must know the binding obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of prayers
Jahr wajib: Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, Jumuah, Eid, Tarawih, Witr. Ikhfa wajib: Zuhr, Asr, third rak'ah of Maghrib, last two of Isha, all rak'ats of Zuhr and Asr.
Note the inclusion of Tarawih and Witr by analogy with Jumuah and Eid.
2
Examine the rationale for the differentiation
Original reasons: At Zuhr and Asr, people could harm the Prophet; at Maghrib they ate; at Isha and Fajr they slept. For Jumuah and Eid, no fear in Madinah.
These are historical circumstances that motivated the practice.
3
Apply the Hanafi legal principle that the ruling persists despite change of cause
Even though Muslims are dominant now, the ruling remains wajib because the persistence of the ruling does not require persistence of the cause. A new reason is people's preoccupation at those times.
This is a key usul point: the ruling can outlive its original 'illa.
4
Identify the dalil and its implications
The dalil is the Prophet's continuous practice (fi'l) and ijma. This makes the ruling wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni al-thubut.
Hanafi principle: continuous practice on an act indicates wujub.
5
Differentiate the imam from the munfarid
The imam has no choice; jahr is wajib. The munfarid has a choice in jahri prayers (may recite loudly or silently). Also, the imam should not strain excessively.
This distinction is crucial for correct practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي تجهر بصلاة الليل وتخافت بصلاة النهار فكان يخافت بعد ذلك في صلاة الظهر والعصر لأنهم كانوا مستعدين للإيذاء في هذين الوقتين ويجهر في المغرب لأنهم كانوا مشغولين بالأكل، العشاء والفجر لكونهم رقوداً. وفي الجمعة والعيدين لأنه أقامهما بالمدينة وما كان للكفار بها قوة. وهذا العذر وإن زال بغلبة المسلمين فالحكم باق لأن بقاءه يستغني عن بقاء السبب ولأنه أخلف عذراً آخر وهو كثرة اشتغال الناس في هاتين الصلاتين دون غيرهما اهـ. وقد انعقد الإجماع على الجهر فيما ذكر وقد قدمنا أن الجهر في هذه المواضع واجب على الإمام للمواظبة من النبي . وتخصيصه بالإمام مفهوم من قوله هنا وخير المنفرد فيما يجهر» فأفاد أن الإمام ليس بمخير قالوا ولا يجهد الإمام نفسه بالجهر. وفي السراج الوهاج : الإمام إذا جهر فوق حاجة الناس فقد أسار وأفاد أنه لا فرق في حق الإمام بين الأداء والقضاء لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء. والحق بالجمعة والعيدين التراويح والوتر في رمضان للتوارث المنقول، والمراد بغيرهما الثالثة من المغرب والأخريان العشاء وجميع ركعات الظهر والعصر.
And he would recite loudly in the night prayer and silently in the day prayer. Then he would recite silently after that in Zuhr and Asr because they were ready to cause harm at those two times. He would recite loudly in Maghrib because they were busy with eating, and in Isha and Fajr because they were asleep. And on Jumuah and the two Eids, because he established them in Madinah and the disbelievers had no power there. And even though this excuse has ceased due to the dominance of Muslims, the ruling remains because its continuance does not require the continuance of the cause, and because another excuse has replaced it, namely the great preoccupation of people at those two prayers unlike others. Ijma has been formed on jahr in what was mentioned, and we have already stated that jahr in these places is obligatory upon the imam due to the constant practice of the Prophet. And its specification to the imam is understood from his saying here: 'And the one praying alone has a choice in what is recited loudly.' So it indicates that the imam is not given a choice. They said, 'And the imam should not strain himself with loud recitation.' And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'If the imam recites louder than necessary, he is sinning.' And it indicates that there is no difference for the imam between performance and make-up, because make-up imitates performance. Included with Jumuah and the two Eids are Tarawih and Witr in Ramadan due to the transmitted continuity. The intended by 'others than these two' is the third rak'ah of Maghrib and the last two of Isha and all rak'ats of Zuhr and Asr.
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about the obligation of jahr (loud recitation) upon the imam in specific prayers. The author begins by explaining the prophetic practice: the Prophet would recite loudly in night prayers (Maghrib, Isha, Fajr) and silently in day prayers (Zuhr, Asr). The reason given is that at the times of Zuhr and Asr, people were active and could cause harm, so silence was safer. At Maghrib, people were busy eating, at Isha and Fajr they were asleep, so loud recitation was appropriate. For Jumuah and Eid, the Prophet established these prayers in Madinah where the disbelievers had no power, so loud recitation was possible. Even though the original reason (fear of harm) no longer exists, the ruling remains because the persistence of the ruling does not require the persistence of the cause; a new reason is the preoccupation of people at those times. The author then states that ijma (consensus) has formed on jahr in these prayers, and it is wajib on the imam due to the Prophet's constant practice. The imam has no choice. However, the munfarid (person praying alone) has a choice in jahri prayers. The author adds that the imam should not strain himself too much. The text also notes that for the imam, the ruling of jahr applies equally to performance and make-up prayer (qada), because qada mimics ada. Finally, it adds that Tarawih and Witr in Ramadan are included with Jumuah and Eid in requiring jahr, based on transmitted practice.

Key Terms
جهر (jahr): Loud recitation in prayer that can be heard by others; obligatory on the imam in specified prayers.
مخافتة (mukhafatah): Silent recitation in prayer; obligatory on the imam in Zuhr, Asr, and other prescribed times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which of the following prayers is jahr (loud recitation) wajib upon the imam according to the Hanafi school?
A) Zuhr and Asr
B) Maghrib and Isha
C) All prayers equally
D) Only Fajr

Key Takeaway
The imam must recite loudly in Maghrib, Isha, Fajr, Jumuah, Eid, Tarawih, and Witr; silently in Zuhr and Asr; this obligation is wajib due to the Prophet's constant practice and ijma.

Salah — Prayer
