Rulings on the Munfarid: Jahr and Ikhfa
Determining the obligation of jahr/ikhfa for one praying alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the munfarid's recitation in silent and loud prayers, identify the qiyas-based evidence, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding sajdah al-sahw.

Core Idea
The munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers; in loud prayers he may choose, but the correct view is that ikhfa is wajib in sirri.

This lesson examines the obligations of loud (jahr) and silent (ikhfa) recitation for the person praying alone (munfarid). While there is a common assumption that the munfarid is free to choose, the Hanafi school holds that ikhfa is obligatory in silent prayers based on a key analogy. The passage also presents an internal dispute about the consequence of violating this obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which act is being ruled upon (the munfarid's recitation in sirri and jahri prayers) and what the ruling is (wajib, mukhayyar, etc.).
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
Find the proof cited: qiyas from the imam's obligation to do ikhfa, with the reasoning 'the munfarid is more entitled'.
The dalil is a qiyas because it draws an analogy between imam and munfarid.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the analogy works: the imam must do ikhfa because his recitation affects others; the munfarid, with no audience, has even less reason to recite loudly.
This is an a fortiori argument (awlā).
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Isam ibn Yusuf and some narrations hold that the munfarid has a choice even in sirri prayers, using the absence of sajdah sahw as evidence.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The text concludes that the correct view (sahih) is that ikhfa is wajib, and that the absence of sajdah sahw does not negate the obligation. The relied-upon position is obligation.
Some later scholars like Halwani and author of al-Khulasah also support no sajdah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أفاد أن المتنفل بالنهار يجب عليه الإخفاء مطلقاً والمتنفل بالليل مخير بين الجهر والإخفاء إن كان منفرداً، أما إن كان إماماً فالجهر واجب كما ذكره الشارح رحمه الله، وأن المنفرد ليس بمخير في الصلاة السرية بل يجب الإخفاء عليه وهو الصحيح لأن الإمام يجب عليه الإخفاء فالمنفرد أولى. وذكر عصام بن يوسف أن المنفرد مخير فيما يخافت فيه أيضاً استدلالاً بعدم وجوب سجود السهو عليه، وتعقبه الشارح بأن الإمام إنما وجب عليه سجود السهو لأن جنايته أعظم لأنه ارتكب الجهر والإسماع بخلاف المنفرد، وتعقبه في فتح القدير بأنا لا ننكر أن واجباً قد يكون أكد من واجب لكن لما لم ينط وجوب السهو إلا بترك الواجب لا بآكد الواجب ولا برتبة مخصوصة منه فحيث كانت المخافتة واجبة على المنفرد ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود. من وفي العناية : إن ظاهر الرواية أن المنفرد مخير فيما يخافت فيه أيضاً وفيه تأمل. والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب . وفي قوله فيما يجهر» دلالة على أن المنفرد مخير في الصلاة الجهرية إذا وفي السراج بعد ذكره التخيير اعتباراً بالفرض قال : والجهر أفضل وعزاه إلى المبسوط. قوله: (ينبغي أن يجب بتركها السجود) قال الشيخ اسمعيل أقول : وجوب سجود السهو على المنفرد إذا جهر فيما يخافت فيه رواية عن أبي حنيفة ذكرت في الذخيرة وغيرها. وفي البرجندي معزياً إلى الظهيرية : وروى أبو سليمان أن المنفرد إذا ظن أنه إمام فجهر كما جهر الإمام يلزمه سجود السهو. ويلائمه ما في المحيط : إذا جهر المنفرد من صلاة المخافتة كان مسيئاً، وفي صلاة الجهر يتخير. كذا في عامة الروايات والذي جزم الحلواني بأنه ظاهر الجواب أنه لا سهو على المنفرد. وفي الخلاصة: لا على المنفرد إذا خافت فيما يجهر به وبالعكس وسيأتي مفصلاً في بابه .اهـ. قلت : ومثله في التتارخانية عن المحيط والذخيرة كما سنذكره في بابه إن شاء الله تعالى قوله : (والظاهر من المذهب الوجوب) فيه سهو فاتت وقضاها نهاراً كما هو حكم الإمام لأن القضاء يحكي الأداء والجهر أفضل وصححه في الذخيرة والخانية واختاره شمس الأئمة في المبسوط وفخر الإسلام، وصحح في الهداية الإخفاء حتماً لأن الجهر ،مختص، أما بالجماعة حتماً أو بالوقت في حق المنفرد على وجه التخيير ولم يوجد أحدهما. وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن الحكم يجوز أن يكون معلولاً بعلل شتى، وعلة الجهر هنا أن القضاء يحكي الأداء بدليل أنه يؤذن ويقيم للقضاء كالأداء. وفي السراج الوهاج : ولو سبق رجل يوم الجمعة بركعة ثم قام لقضاء ما فاته كان بالخيار إن شاء جهر وإن شاء خافت كالمنفرد في صلاة الفجر. وفي الخلاصة عن الأصل: رجل يصلي وحده فجاء رجل واقتدى به بعدما قرأ الفاتحة أو بعضها يقرأ الفاتحة ثانياً ويجهر اهـ. يعني إذا كانت الصلاة جهرية ولم يجهر المصلي، ووجهه أن الجهر فيما بقي صار واجباً بالاقتداء، والجمع بين الجهر والمخافتة في ركعة واحدة شنيع، وقيد المصنف بالقراءة لأن ما عداها من الأذكار فيه تفصيل إن كان ذكراً وجب للصلاة فإنه يجهر به كتكبيرة الافتتاح وما ليس بفرض وضع للعلامة فإنه يجهر به كتكبيرات الانتقال عند كل خفض ورفع إذا كان إماماً، إما المنفرد والمقتدي فلا يجهران به وإن كان يختص ببعض الصلاة كتكبيرات العيدين جهر به، ذلك وكذا القنوت في مذهب العراقيين واختار صاحب الهداية الإخفاء به، وإما ما سوی فما فلا يجهر به مثل التشهد وآمين والتسبيحات لأنها أذكار لا يقصد بها العلامة. كذا في السراج والوهاج. ولم يبين المصنف حد الجهر والإخفاء للاختلاف مع اختلاف التصحيح، فذهب الكرخي إلى أن أدنى الجهر أن يسمع نفسه، وأدنى المخافتة تصحيح الحروف. وفي البدائع :
And it indicates that the one performing voluntary prayer during the day must conceal absolutely, and the one performing voluntary prayer at night has a choice between loud and silent if he is alone, but if he is an imam then loud recitation is obligatory as the commentator stated. And that the one praying alone is not given a choice in silent prayer, rather concealment is obligatory upon him, and that is the correct view, because the imam is obligated to conceal, so the one alone is more entitled. And Isam ibn Yusuf mentioned that the one alone is given a choice in what is concealed as well, deducing from the absence of obligation of sajdah al-sahw upon him. The commentator rebutted him by saying that the imam is obligated to perform sajdah al-sahw because his violation is greater, as he committed loud recitation and made others hear, unlike the one alone. And this was rebutted in Fath al-Qadir by saying: we do not deny that an obligation may be more emphatic than another obligation, but since the obligation of sajdah is only necessitated by leaving an obligation, not by a more emphatic obligation nor by a specific rank, so where concealment is obligatory upon the one alone, sajdah should be required by leaving it. From al-Inayah: The apparent of the riwayah is that the one alone has a choice in what is concealed as well, and there is reflection on it. The apparent from the madhhab is obligation. And in his statement 'in what is recited loudly' there is indication that the one alone has a choice in loud prayer. And in al-Siraj after mentioning the choice, considering the obligatory, he said: 'And loud is better' and attributed it to al-Mabsut. His statement: 'Sajdah should be required by leaving it' – Sheikh Ismail said: I say: The obligation of sajdah al-sahw on the one alone if he recites loudly in what should be concealed is a narration from Abu Hanifah mentioned in al-Dhakhirah and others. And in al-Birjandi, attributed to al-Zahiriyyah: And Abu Sulayman narrated that if the one alone thinks he is an imam and recites loudly as the imam does, sajdah al-sahw becomes obligatory upon him. And what is in al-Muhit is consistent: if the one alone recites loudly in a silent prayer, he is sinning, and in loud prayer he has a choice. This is in most narrations. What Halwani decisively stated is that the apparent answer is that there is no sajdah on the one alone. And in al-Khulasah: There is no sajdah on the one alone if he conceals in what is recited loudly and vice versa. And it will come in detail in its chapter. I said: And similar is in al-Tatarkhaniyyah from al-Muhit and al-Dhakhirah as we will mention in its chapter if Allah wills. His statement: 'And the apparent from the madhhab is obligation' – there is an oversight in it. If one misses a prayer and makes it up during the day, his ruling is like that of the imam because the make-up imitates the performance, and loud is better. This was corrected in al-Dhakhirah and al-Khaniyyah, and chosen by Shams al-Aimmah in al-Mabsut and Fakhr al-Islam. But al-Hidayah corrected concealment as mandatory because loud is specific either to congregation as mandatory or to time for the one alone by way of choice, and neither exists. It was rebutted in Ghayat al-Bayan that a ruling can be caused by various causes, and the cause for loud here is that the make-up imitates the performance, as evidence by the fact that one gives adhan and iqamah for make-up like for performance. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If a man on Friday is preceded by one rak'ah and then stands to make up what he missed, he has a choice: if he wishes he recites loudly and if he wishes silently, like the one alone in Fajr prayer. And in al-Khulasah from al-Asl: A man praying alone, another man comes and follows him after he has recited al-Fatihah or part of it – he recites al-Fatihah a second time and recites loudly. Meaning if the prayer was loud and the one praying had not recited loudly. The reason is that loud in the remaining part has become obligatory due to the following, and combining loud and silent in one rak'ah is repulsive. The author specified recitation because as for other remembrances, there is detail: if it is a dhikr obligatory for the prayer, he recites it loudly like the opening takbir; and what is not obligatory is placed as a sign, so he recites it loudly like the takbirs of transition at every lowering and raising, if he is an imam. As for the one alone and the follower, they do not recite them loudly. And if it is specific to a part of the prayer like the takbirs of the two Eids, he recites them loudly. Likewise, qunut in the school of the Iraqis, while the author of al-Hidayah chose concealment for it. As for other than that, he does not recite loudly, like tashahhud, amin, and tasbihat, because they are remembrances not intended as signs. Thus in al-Siraj and al-Wahhaj. The author did not define the limit of loud and silent recitation due to differences in verification. al-Karkhi held that the minimum of loudness is that he hears himself, and the minimum of silence is correct pronunciation of letters. And in al-Bada'i:
Source pages p. 586

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof about the obligations of jahr and ikhfa for the munfarid (one praying alone). It opens by stating that a person performing voluntary prayer during the day must conceal (ikhfa) absolutely. At night, the munfarid has a choice between jahr and ikhfa, but if he is an imam, jahr is wajib. The correct view (sahih) is that the munfarid must do ikhfa in silent prayers (sirri), because the imam must do ikhfa, and the munfarid is even more entitled. However, Isam ibn Yusuf held that the munfarid has a choice even in silent prayers, deducing from the absence of sajdah sahw. The commentator rebutted that the imam's violation is greater. Then a rebuttal from Fath al-Qadir argues that since sajdah sahw is caused by leaving an obligation, if ikhfa is obligatory on the munfarid, then leaving it should require sajdah. The text then cites various sources: al-Inayah says the apparent riwayah gives choice, but the madhhab's apparent leaning is obligation. Al-Siraj reports that jahr is better. Sheikh Ismail cites a narration from Abu Hanifah that if the munfarid does jahr in a sirri prayer, sajdah sahw is obligatory. Abu Sulayman narrates that if the munfarid thinks he is an imam and does jahr, sajdah is necessary. Al-Muhit says the munfarid is sinning if he does jahr in sirri, but has choice in jahri. Halwani decided there is no sajdah on the munfarid. Al-Khulasah agrees. The author then notes that the statement 'the apparent from the madhhab is obligation' contains an oversight. The text then discusses the ruling on qada of a missed prayer made up during the day: some say jahr is better, others say ikhfa is mandatory because jahr is specific to congregation or time. Al-Hidayah favors ikhfa, but Ghayat al-Bayan rebuts that the cause for jahr is that qada imitates ada. Finally, a scenario is given: if a man catches up in congregation on Friday, he has a choice. Also, if a person praying alone is joined by another, he must repeat al-Fatihah loudly because following makes jahr obligatory. The passage ends by distinguishing which recitations are done loudly: obligatory ones like takbirat al-iftitah, and those placed as signs like transition takbirs; but tashahhud, amin, and tasbihat are not loud. The author does not define the limits of jahr and ikhfa, but cites al-Karkhi's definitions.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): One who prays alone, not in congregation.
سجود السهو (sajdah al-sahw): Prostration for forgetfulness due to leaving an obligatory act or committing an error in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what is the ruling on the munfarid (person praying alone) in a silent prayer (sirri)?
A) He may choose jahr or ikhfa
B) Jahr is obligatory
C) Ikhfa is obligatory
D) He must recite silently if he is an imam, but has choice otherwise

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the munfarid must recite silently in silent prayers; this obligation is proven by qiyas from the imam's obligation, even though sajdah al-sahw may not be required for its violation.

Definition of Minimum Jah and Ikhfa in Recitation
Definition ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of adna al-jahr and adna al-mukhafata as defined by Imam al-Karkhi and distinguish between them.

Core Idea
The minimum for loud recitation is self-hearing; silence is merely correct letter pronunciation.

This lesson clarifies the technical juristic definitions of jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa (silent recitation) according to the Hanafi school. Understanding these thresholds is essential for determining when the obligatory recitation in prayer has been fulfilled correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify what is being defined
The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq did not specify the exact limit due to differing methods of verification.
2
State al-Karkhi's definition of jahr
The minimum for jahr is that the reciter hears himself if he listens.
3
State al-Karkhi's definition of ikhfa
The minimum for ikhfa is correct pronunciation of letters (movement of tongue and lips), regardless of audible sound.
4
Understand the legal implication
If the reciter fails to hear himself when jahr is required, the requirement is not fulfilled. For ikhfa, only correct articulation matters.
5
Note the continuation
The passage ends with 'Wa fi al-Bada'i' indicating further discussion in al-Bada'i' al-Sana'i'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يبين المصنف حد الجهر والإخفاء للاختلاف مع اختلاف التصحيح، فذهب الكرخي إلى أن أدنى الجهر أن يسمع نفسه، وأدنى المخافتة تصحيح الحروف. وفي البدائع :
And the author did not specify the limit of loudness and silence due to differences according to different corrections. Al-Karkhi held that the minimum of loudness is that he hears himself, and the minimum of silence is correct pronunciation of letters. And in al-Bada'i:
Source pages p. 587

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling that presents the Hanafi technical definitions of the threshold between jahr (loud recitation) and ikhfa (silent recitation). The author of the matn (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not specify the exact limit due to differences among scholars in verifying the definitions. The text then quotes Imam al-Karkhi's definition: the minimum for jahr (loudness) is that the reciter can hear himself if he listens; the minimum for ikhfa (silence) is that he pronounces the letters correctly (i.e., the movements of his tongue and lips are correct, even if no sound is heard by himself). This distinction is important for determining when the obligation of jahr or ikhfa is fulfilled. The passage then cuts off with 'Wa fi al-Bada'i', indicating that other definitions exist in al-Bada'i' al-Sana'i' and other works. The Hanafi school relies on these definitions to determine the validity of prayer in terms of recitation.

Key Terms
أدنى الجهر (adna al-jahr): The minimum threshold for loud recitation: that the reciter hears himself if he listens.
أدنى المخافتة (adna al-mukhafatah): The minimum threshold for silent recitation: correct pronunciation of letters (حركات اللسان والشفتين) without necessarily producing audible sound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) That others within the congregation can hear
B) That the reciter hears himself if he listens
C) That the reciter sees his lips move
D) That the recitation is audible to the imam alone

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines jahr as self-hearing and ikhfa as correct articulation of letters.

Salah — Prayer

Defining Loud and Silent Recitation: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on defining jahr and mukhafatah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi definitions of jahr and mukhāfatah and explain the intra-madhhab disagreements and their practical consequences.

Core Idea
Silent prayer requires making yourself hear; mere tongue movement without sound is insufficient.

The Hanafi school has a rich internal debate on what exactly constitutes loud (jahr) and silent (mukhāfatah) recitation in prayer. While the majority and the relied-upon position require actual audibility (to oneself for silent, to others for loud), some early Hanafis argued that mere articulation of letters suffices. This lesson unpacks the different views, their proofs, and why the school settled on al-Hinduwani's definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rulings and Their Scope
State the acts involved: jahr and mukhāfatah in prayer, and related acts like divorce and oaths where audibility matters.
The same definitions apply to all utterances in Hanafi fiqh.
2
State the Relied-Upon Position
Learn al-Hinduwani's definition: jahr is to make others hear, mukhāfatah is to make oneself hear.
This is the mufta bihi (operative for fatwa).
3
Map the Intra-Hanafi Disagreements
Identify the alternative views: al-Karkhi (articulation without sound suffices), Bishr al-Marisi (must be such that it could be heard), al-Fadli (jahr is to make everyone hear).
Each view has a different dalil and practical outcome.
4
Analyze the Proofs and Responses
Examine the reasoning (qiyas vs. istihsan) behind each view and why the majority rejected al-Karkhi's analogy.
Sound is integral to speech; letters are qualities of sound.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence and Fatwa
Apply the mufta bihi to concrete scenarios: validity of prayer for one who cannot hear himself (deaf, noisy environment).
The mufta bihi avoids hardship and preserves the integrity of recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما قاله الكرخي أقيس وأصح. وفي كتاب الصلاة لمحمد إشارة إليه فإنه قال : إن شاء قرأ في نفسه وإن شاء جهر وأسمع نفسه .اهـ. وأكثر المشايخ على أن الصحيح أن الجهر أن يسمع غيره والمخافتة أن يسمع نفسه وهو قول الهندواني، وكذا كل ما يتعلق بالنطق كالتسمية على الذبيحة ووجوب السجدة بالتلاوة والعتاق والطلاق والاستثناء حتى لو طلق ولم يسمع نفسه لا يقع وإن صحح الحروف. وفي الخلاصة : الإمام إذا قرأ في صلاة المخافتة بحيث سمع رجل أو رجلان لا يكون جهراً والجهر أن يسمع الكل .اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : واعلم أن القراءة وإن كانت فعل اللسان لكن فعله الذي هو كلام والكلام بالحروف والحروف كيفية تعرض للصوت وهو أخص من النفس فإن النفس المعروض بالفرع فالحرف عارض للصوت لا للنفس فمجرد تصحيحها بلا صوت إيمان إلى الحروف بعضلات المخارج لا حروف فلا كلام بقي أن هذا لا يقتضي أن يلزم في مفهوم القراءة أن يصل إلى السمع بل كونه بحيث يسمع وهو قول بشر المريسي، ولعله المراد بقول الهندواني بناء على أن الظاهر سماعه بعد وجود الصوت إذا لم يكن مانع اهـ. فاختار أن قول بشر والهندواني متحدان وهو خلاف الظاهر، بل الظاهر من عباراتهم أن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال قال الكرخي : إن القراءة تصحيح الحروف وإن لم يكن الصوت المخافتة أن يسمع نفسه أن يكون أعلاها أن يسمع يسمع غيره كما قاله بعضهم، فيكون إسماع الغير جهراً ومخافتة وفيه نظر، بل يلزم أن يكون أعلاها تصحيح الحروف مع أنه قول الكرخي، ولعله لهذا. والله تعالى أعلم لم يذكر ذلك صاحب الهداية في القول الثاني لكن في القهستاني أن في قوله «وأدنى المخافتة إسماع نفسه إشعاراً بأن أعلى المخافتة تصحيح الحروف فقط، وهذا قول الكرخي وأبي بكر الأعمش، وروي عن محمد وأبي الحسن الثوري وأبي نصر بن سلام فزاد «أدنى» إشارة إلى أن قول هؤلاء الأئمة غير ساقط عن حيز الاعتبار أصلاً .اهـ. فليتأمل. وقد يجاب عن الأول بأن أعلى المخافتة ليس أن يسمع نفسه بل أن يقرأ في قلبه بلا تحريك لسان وهو الظاهر، ويؤيده ما في شرح الشيخ إسمعيل عن شرح الطحاوي ولو قرأ بقلبه ولم يحرك لسانه فإنه لا يجوز، ولو حرك لسانه بالحروف أجزأه وإن كان لا يسمع منه اهـ. قوله : (والجهر أن يسمع الكل قال في النهر : هذا مشكل وجعله في المعراج قول الفضلي وكأنه اختيار له .اهـ. أقول : ذكر في المعراج الفضلي مع الهندواني وسيأتي عن المجتبى أنه لا يجزىء عند الهندواني ما لم تسمع أذناه ومن بقربه، وعلى هذا فالمراد بقول الخلاصة بحيث سمع رجل أو رجلان ممن بقربه وبقولها الجهر أن يسمع الكل أي من ليس بقربه، وليس المراد كل فرد لأنه قد يكون متعذراً أو متعسراً فظهر أن ما في الخلاصة لا إشكال فيه بل هو جارٍ على قول الهندواني والفضلي، واندفع ما قيل إنه قول آخر غير الثلاثة الآتية تدبر قوله : (إن في المسألة ثلاثة أقوال) أقول : وبه صرح في النهاية ومعراج الدراية، ولكن قد يقال : يتعين ما قاله الكمال لأنه قد يحصل مانع من إسماع نفسه فيلزم أن لا يكون مخافتة إلا برفع صوته جداً وهو بعيد على أنه قد يكون ومن بقربه بحيث يسمع، وقال بشر : لا بد أن يكون بحيث يسمع. وقال الهندواني : لا بد أن يكون أذناه مسموعاً له. زاد في المجتبى في النقل عن الهندواني أنه لا يجزئه ما لم يسمع اهـ. ونقل في الذخيرة عن الحلواني أن الأصح هذا، ولا ينبغي أن يجعل قولاً رابعاً بل هو قول الهندواني الأول. وفي العادة إن ما كان مسموعاً له يكون مسموعاً لمن هو بقربه أيضاً. وفي الذخيرة معزياً إلى القاضي علاء الدين في شرح مختلفاته أن الأصح عندي أن في بعض التصرفات يكتفي بسماعه وفي بعض التصرفات يشترط سماع غيره مثلاً في البيع لو أدنى المشتري صماخه إلى فم البائع وسمع يكفي ولو سمع البائع بنفسه ولم يسمعه المشتري لا يكفي. وفيما إذا حلف لا يكلم فلاناً فناداه من بعيد بحيث لا يسمع لا يحنث في يمينه . نص على هذا في كتاب الإيمان لأن شرط الحنث وجود الكلام قوله : (ولو) ترك السورة في أولي العشاء قرأها في الأخريين مع الفاتحة جهراً ولو ترك الفاتحة (لا) أي لا يقرؤها في الأخريين وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يقضي واحدة منهما لأن الواجب إذا فات عن وقته لا يقضي إلا بدليل. ولهما وهو الفرق بين الوجهين أن قراءة الفاتحة شرعت على وجه يترتب عليها السورة فلو قضاها في الأخريين بعد أن لم يوجد اهـ . أصم فيقال عليه ما حقيقة المخافتة في حقه. ويدل على هذا أنه اشترط في الجهر إسماع غيره وكيف يسوغ القول بأنه على ظاهره حتى لو كان إماماً وكان ثم مانع من سماع صوته أو كان من اقتدى به أصم هل يقال إنه ترك الجهر الواجب وصلاته ناقصة ؟ والذي يغلب على الظن أنه لا يقول به أحد. ثم رأيت العلامة خير الدين الرملي بحث في فتاواه بنحو ما قلته والله تعالى الحمد وذلك حيث قال البحر : هذا ودعوى خلاف الظاهر لما قاله الكمال بعيد إذا أغلب الشراح لم ينقلوا في المسألة قولاً ثالثاً، بل اقتصروا على ذكر قول الكرخي والهندواني مع ظهور وجه ما قاله الكمال وكونه وسطاً إذ يبعد اشتراط حقيقة السماع مع العلم بأنه يختلف باختلاف آلته، وبما تخلف مع حقيقة الجهر ولا بد من إرادته تقليلاً للأقوال بل إن ادعى وجوب المصير إليه فهو متجه بدليل أن من به صمم لا نفسه إلا باستعمال ما هو جهر في حق غيره وقد لا يتهيأ معه له ذلك مع ما فيه من الرفق يسمع وعدم الحرج فإنه مع التعويل على قول الهندواني وعدم اعتبار ما سواه من الأقوال لو أخذ فيه هذا الشرط لزم عدم صحة أكثر الصلوات من كل خاص وعام فتبين صحة ما استظهره الكمال بن الهمام، والمحل محتمل لزيادة البحث ولكن الاقتصار على ما ذكرنا أولى لأن الإسماع تضرب عما فيه إطالة وإن تعلق بمبحث السماع والحاصل أن يقال في المسألة قولان : قول للكرخي وقول للهندواني والاعتماد على قول الهندواني والله تعالى أعلم قوله : ( وفي بعض التصرفات يشترط الخ) حرر في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي والمحيط أنه ضعيف وأن الصحيح قول الشيخين - أعني الهندواني والفضلي - قوله : (فلو قضاها في الأخريين تترتب الفاتحة على السورة إذ التقدير أنه قرأ السورة ثم يقضي الفاتحة
What al-Karkhi said is more analogically sound and correct. In the book of prayer by Muhammad there is an indication to it, for he said: If he wishes he may recite in himself, and if he wishes he may recite aloud and make himself hear. End. Most of the mashayikh hold that the correct view is that jahr is to make others hear, and mukhafatah is to make oneself hear, and that is the saying of al-Hinduwani. Likewise everything related to utterance, like the tasmiyah over the slaughtered animal, the obligation of prostration upon recitation, manumission, divorce, and exception; so much so that if he divorces and does not hear himself, it does not occur even if he articulates the letters correctly. In al-Khulasah: If the imam recites in a silent prayer such that one or two men hear, it is not jahr; jahr is that everyone hears. End. In Fath al-Qadir: Know that recitation, although it is an action of the tongue, its actual action is speech, and speech is by letters, and letters are a quality that occurs to sound, and it is more specific than breath, for breath is what is presented to the branch, so the letter occurs to sound not to breath, so mere articulation without sound is a confirmation of the letters by the muscles of the articulation points, not letters, so there is no speech. It remains that this does not entail that in the concept of recitation it must reach the hearing, but rather it being such that it could be heard, and that is the saying of Bishr al-Marisi, and perhaps that is what al-Hinduwani meant, based on the apparent hearing after the existence of sound if there is no hindrance. End. So he chose that the saying of Bishr and al-Hinduwani are the same, which is contrary to the apparent. Rather, the apparent from their expressions is that there are three sayings in the issue. Al-Karkhi said: Recitation is the articulation of letters even if there is no sound. Mukhafatah is to make oneself hear, and its highest is to make oneself hear, or to make others hear as some said, so making others hear would be jahr and mukhafatah, but there is consideration in this. Rather, it would entail that its highest is articulation of letters, while that is the saying of al-Karkhi. Perhaps for this reason, the author of al-Hidayah did not mention that as the second saying. But in al-Qahistani there is an indication in his saying 'the minimum of mukhafatah is making oneself hear' that the maximum of mukhafatah is merely articulating letters, and that is the saying of al-Karkhi and Abu Bakr al-A'mash, and it is narrated from Muhammad, Abu al-Hasan al-Thawri, and Abu Nasr ibn Salam, so he added 'minimum' to indicate that the saying of these imams is not completely out of consideration. End. So let it be pondered. It may be answered regarding the first that the maximum of mukhafatah is not making oneself hear, but rather reciting in the heart without moving the tongue, and that is apparent. This is supported by what is in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il from the commentary of al-Tahawi: If he recites with his heart and does not move his tongue, it is not permissible; if he moves his tongue with the letters, it suffices even if he does not hear from it. End. His saying: (Jahr is to make everyone hear). In al-Nahr: This is problematic, and he made it in al-Mi'raj the saying of al-Fadli, as if it is his choice. End. I say: He mentioned in al-Mi'raj al-Fadli along with al-Hinduwani, and it will come from al-Mujtaba that it is not valid according to al-Hinduwani unless his ears and those near him hear. Based on this, the meaning of the saying of al-Khulasah 'such that one or two men hear' refers to those near him, and its saying 'jahr is to make everyone hear' means those not near him, not every individual because that may be impossible or difficult. So it appears that what is in al-Khulasah is not problematic; rather, it agrees with the saying of al-Hinduwani and al-Fadli, and it repels what was said that it is another saying besides the three. Ponder. His saying: (There are three sayings in the issue) I say: This is stated in al-Nihayah and Mi'raj al-Dirayah. But it may be said: What al-Kamal said is determined because there may be a hindrance preventing one from hearing himself, which would necessitate that mukhafatah would not be except by raising his voice very high, which is unlikely. And it may be that there is someone near him who hears? And Bishr said: It must be such that he hears. Al-Hinduwani said: It must be that his ears hear it. In al-Mujtaba, it is added in the transmission from al-Hinduwani that it does not suffice unless he hears. End. In al-Dhakhirah from al-Halwani that the correct is this, and it should not be considered a fourth saying; rather, it is al-Hinduwani's first saying. Habitually, what is heard by him is also heard by those near him. In al-Dhakhirah, attributed to al-Qadi 'Ala' al-Din in his commentary on his Mukhtalifat: The correct in my view is that in some actions, hearing by oneself suffices, and in some actions, hearing by others is required. For example, in a sale, if the buyer puts his ear to the seller's mouth and hears, it suffices; if the seller hears himself and the buyer does not hear, it does not suffice. And if one swears not to speak to someone, and calls him from afar such that he does not hear, he does not break his oath. This is textually stated in the book of oaths because the condition of breaking the oath is the existence of speech. His saying: (If he leaves the surah in the first two of 'Isha, he recites it in the last two with the Fatiha aloud, and if he leaves the Fatiha, no) i.e., he does not recite it in the last two. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not make up either of them because when an obligation misses its time, it is not made up except by evidence. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and the distinction between the two cases is that the recitation of the Fatiha is prescribed in a manner that the surah is dependent on it; if he makes it up in the last two after it was not present... A deaf person: It is said regarding him: What is the reality of mukhafatah in his case? This is indicated by the fact that he required in jahr the hearing of others. How can it be said that it is taken literally, such that if the imam has a hindrance to his voice being heard, or the follower is deaf, would it be said that he has left the obligatory jahr and his prayer is deficient? It is most likely that no one would say this. Then I saw the scholar Khayr al-Din al-Ramli discussing in his Fatawa similar to what I said, and praise be to Allah. That is where al-Bahr said: This claim of being contrary to the apparent due to what al-Kamal said is far-fetched, since most of the commentators did not transmit a third saying in the issue; rather, they limited themselves to mentioning the saying of al-Karkhi and al-Hinduwani, along with the apparent aspect of what al-Kamal said and it being a middle way. For it is unlikely to require the reality of hearing while knowing that it varies according to the instrument, and what is lacking with the reality of jahr, and it must be intended to reduce the number of sayings. Rather, if one claims that it is obligatory to adopt it, it is sound, as evidenced by the case of one who is deaf: he cannot hear himself except by using what is jahr for others, and that may not be possible for him. Besides, there is leniency in hearing and no hardship. For relying on the saying of al-Hinduwani and disregarding other sayings, if this condition is adopted, it would lead to most prayers being invalid for both the elite and the common, so the correctness of what al-Kamal ibn al-Humam deduced becomes clear. The matter is open to further discussion, but confining to what we have mentioned is better because the discussion about hearing would prolong it. The summary is that there are two sayings in the issue: a saying of al-Karkhi and a saying of al-Hinduwani, and reliance is on the saying of al-Hinduwani. Allah knows best. His saying: (In some actions, it is required, etc.) It is established in al-Shurnublaliyyah from al-Kafi and al-Muhit that it is weak, and the correct is the saying of the two shaykhs – meaning al-Hinduwani and al-Fadli. His saying: (If he makes it up in the last two, the Fatiha would be consequent upon the surah, as if he recited the surah then makes up the Fatiha.
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion (sharh) on the definition of jahr (loud recitation) and mukhafatah (silent recitation) in prayer, which is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author begins by presenting al-Karkhi's view that recitation is merely articulating letters correctly, even without sound. Then he mentions that most mashayikh follow al-Hinduwani's view: jahr is to make others hear, and mukhafatah is to make oneself hear. This ruling applies to all utterances related to prayer and other acts like divorce and oaths. The text then cites al-Khulasah and Fath al-Qadir to elaborate, noting that some scholars like Bishr al-Marisi require that the sound be such that it could be heard, while al-Hinduwani requires actual hearing by oneself. The author reconciles the views and notes that al-Kamal ibn al-Humam proposed a middle ground: the minimum of mukhafatah is to make oneself hear, but the maximum is mere articulation. However, the preferred position (mufta bihi) as stated at the end is the saying of al-Hinduwani, with the condition that one hears himself and those near him, because a rigid requirement would invalidate many prayers. The passage also includes a discussion on the case of a deaf person, where the reality of mukhafatah is defined according to his ability. The commentary emphasizes that the relied-upon view is that of al-Hinduwani, and the other opinions are weak.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation that makes others hear, according to the relied-upon view.
المخافتة (al-mukhāfatah): Silent recitation that makes oneself hear, according to the relied-upon view.
تصحيح الحروف (taṣḥīḥ al-ḥurūf): Articulating letters correctly even without sound, considered sufficient by al-Karkhi.
السماع (al-samā'): Hearing: the condition for valid recitation in the relied-upon view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the minimum requirement for valid mukhāfatah (silent recitation) in prayer?
A) Articulating the letters correctly without moving the tongue.
B) Moving the tongue with the letters even if no sound is heard.
C) Making oneself hear the recitation.
D) Making everyone in the mosque hear.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that mukhāfatah requires making oneself hear; jahr requires making others hear, with leniency for those who cannot hear.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Reciting Missed Surah or Fatiha in Later Rak'ahs of 'Isha
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada' of missed recitation in 'Isha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on making up missed recitation in 'Isha prayer and apply the distinction between missing al-Fatiha and missing the surah.

Core Idea
A missed surah can be made up later; a missed al-Fatiha cannot — because al-Fatiha has a fixed sequential place.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about compensating for missed recitation in the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha prayer. The disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad on one side and Abu Yusuf on the other reveals a key legal principle: some obligations can be relocated if missed, but a pillar with a specific order (tartib) cannot be retroactively inserted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and omission
Determine what was omitted: the surah after al-Fatiha, or al-Fatiha itself, in the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha (where recitation is aloud).
2
State the main Hanafi position
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: if the surah is missed, it is recited in the last two rak'ahs with al-Fatiha aloud; if al-Fatiha is missed, it is not made up at all.
3
Note Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf argues that neither is made up, because any wajib missed in its proper time cannot be compensated without specific textual evidence.
This is a stricter principle emphasizing the time-bound nature of obligations.
4
Understand the rationale for distinction
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad distinguish: al-Fatiha is prescribed to be followed by the surah; if al-Fatiha is missed, inserting it later would reverse the order (surah before Fatiha). The surah, being dependent on al-Fatiha, can be relocated as it is an additional element.
The key is the sequential dependency (tartib).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to the relied-upon view, if one misses the surah, he recites it in the last two rak'ahs; if he misses al-Fatiha, he does not compensate, and the prayer is valid with sajdah sahw (or without, according to some).
Abu Yusuf's view would absolve the worshipper from any compensatory recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) ترك السورة في أولي العشاء قرأها في الأخريين مع الفاتحة جهراً ولو ترك الفاتحة (لا) أي لا يقرؤها في الأخريين وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف : لا يقضي واحدة منهما لأن الواجب إذا فات عن وقته لا يقضي إلا بدليل. ولهما وهو الفرق بين الوجهين أن قراءة الفاتحة شرعت على وجه يترتب عليها السورة فلو قضاها في الأخريين بعد أن لم يوجد اهـ . أصم فيقال عليه ما حقيقة المخافتة في حقه. ويدل على هذا أنه اشترط في الجهر إسماع غيره وكيف يسوغ القول بأنه على ظاهره حتى لو كان إماماً وكان ثم مانع من سماع صوته أو كان من اقتدى به أصم هل يقال إنه ترك الجهر الواجب وصلاته ناقصة ؟ والذي يغلب على الظن أنه لا يقول به أحد. ثم رأيت العلامة خير الدين الرملي بحث في فتاواه بنحو ما قلته والله تعالى الحمد وذلك حيث قال البحر : هذا ودعوى خلاف الظاهر لما قاله الكمال بعيد إذا أغلب الشراح لم ينقلوا في المسألة قولاً ثالثاً، بل اقتصروا على ذكر قول الكرخي والهندواني مع ظهور وجه ما قاله الكمال وكونه وسطاً إذ يبعد اشتراط حقيقة السماع مع العلم بأنه يختلف باختلاف آلته، وبما تخلف مع حقيقة الجهر ولا بد من إرادته تقليلاً للأقوال بل إن ادعى وجوب المصير إليه فهو متجه بدليل أن من به صمم لا نفسه إلا باستعمال ما هو جهر في حق غيره وقد لا يتهيأ معه له ذلك مع ما فيه من الرفق يسمع وعدم الحرج فإنه مع التعويل على قول الهندواني وعدم اعتبار ما سواه من الأقوال لو أخذ فيه هذا الشرط لزم عدم صحة أكثر الصلوات من كل خاص وعام فتبين صحة ما استظهره الكمال بن الهمام، والمحل محتمل لزيادة البحث ولكن الاقتصار على ما ذكرنا أولى لأن الإسماع تضرب عما فيه إطالة وإن تعلق بمبحث السماع والحاصل أن يقال في المسألة قولان : قول للكرخي وقول للهندواني والاعتماد على قول الهندواني والله تعالى أعلم قوله : ( وفي بعض التصرفات يشترط الخ) حرر في الشرنبلالية عن الكافي والمحيط أنه ضعيف وأن الصحيح قول الشيخين - أعني الهندواني والفضلي - قوله : (فلو قضاها في الأخريين تترتب الفاتحة على السورة إذ التقدير أنه قرأ السورة ثم يقضي الفاتحة
His saying: (If) he leaves the surah in the first two of 'Isha, he recites it in the last two with the Fatiha aloud, and if he leaves the Fatiha, (no) i.e., he does not recite it in the last two. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not make up either of them because when an obligation misses its time, it is not made up except by evidence. For them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), and the distinction between the two cases is that the recitation of the Fatiha is prescribed in a manner that the surah is dependent on it; if he makes it up in the last two after it was not present... How can it be said that it is taken literally, such that if the imam has a hindrance to his voice being heard, or the follower is deaf, would it be said that he has left the obligatory jahr and his prayer is deficient? It is most likely that no one would say this. Then I saw the scholar Khayr al-Din al-Ramli discussing in his Fatawa similar to what I said, and praise be to Allah. That is where al-Bahr said: This claim of being contrary to the apparent due to what al-Kamal said is far-fetched, since most of the commentators did not transmit a third saying in the issue; rather, they limited themselves to mentioning the saying of al-Karkhi and al-Hinduwani, along with the apparent aspect of what al-Kamal said and it being a middle way. For it is unlikely to require the reality of hearing while knowing that it varies according to the instrument, and what is lacking with the reality of jahr, and it must be intended to reduce the number of sayings. Rather, if one claims that it is obligatory to adopt it, it is sound, as evidenced by the case of one who is deaf: he cannot hear himself except by using what is jahr for others, and that may not be possible for him. Besides, there is leniency in hearing and no hardship. For relying on the saying of al-Hinduwani and disregarding other sayings, if this condition is adopted, it would lead to most prayers being invalid for both the elite and the common, so the correctness of what al-Kamal ibn al-Humam deduced becomes clear. The matter is open to further discussion, but confining to what we have mentioned is better because the discussion about hearing would prolong it. The summary is that there are two sayings in the issue: a saying of al-Karkhi and a saying of al-Hinduwani, and reliance is on the saying of al-Hinduwani. Allah knows best. His saying: (In some actions, it is required, etc.) It is established in al-Shurnublaliyyah from al-Kafi and al-Muhit that it is weak, and the correct is the saying of the two shaykhs – meaning al-Hinduwani and al-Fadli. His saying: (If he makes it up in the last two, the Fatiha would be consequent upon the surah, as if he recited the surah then makes up the Fatiha.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific ruling: If a person omits the additional surah (after al-Fatiha) in the first two rak'ahs of 'Isha prayer, he should recite that surah in the last two rak'ahs along with al-Fatiha, and he recites it aloud. However, if he omits al-Fatiha itself in the first two rak'ahs, he does not make it up in the last two – according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf disagrees and says that if any obligatory recitation is missed in its proper time, it is not made up later without specific evidence. The distinction drawn by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is that al-Fatiha is prescribed in such a way that the surah is dependent on it (the surah follows al-Fatiha in sequence). Therefore, if one misses al-Fatiha, he cannot insert it retroactively in the last two because that would disrupt the order (al-Fatiha should come before the surah). But if the surah is missed, it can be read later because it is merely an addition. The passage then digresses into a discussion about the definition of jahr and mukhafatah (which was covered in the previous lesson), but the core issue here is the qadā' of missed recitation. The commentary concludes that the relied-upon view is that of al-Hinduwani for the jahr/mukhafatah definition, and by extension, the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is the mufta bihi for this issue, as Abu Yusuf's view is weaker.

Key Terms
أولى العشاء (ūlayā al-ʿishā'): The first two rak'ahs of the 'Isha prayer.
الأخريين (al-ukhrawayn): The last two rak'ahs of the 'Isha prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the reason given by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad for not making up a missed al-Fatiha in the last two rak'ahs?
A) Because al-Fatiha is a sunnah, not a wajib.
B) Because it would disrupt the sequential order with the surah.
C) Because its time is past and it cannot be relocated.
D) Because Abu Yusuf objected to it.

Key Takeaway
According to the relied-upon view, a missed surah must be made up aloud in the last two rak'ahs; a missed al-Fatiha is not compensated because it would disrupt the prescribed sequence.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Ruling on Making Up Missed Surah in 'Isha Prayer
Expansion on qada' of missed recitation in 'Isha prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on making up a missed Surah in 'Isha prayer and explain why the relied-upon position is recommendation (mustahabb) not obligation.

Core Idea
Making up a missed Surah is recommended, not obligatory, despite contrary wording in some Hanafi texts.

A worshipper forgets to recite the Surah after the Fatiha in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha. What should he do? The Hanafi school has multiple opinions on this, but the later relied-upon position is that he should recite it in the last two rak'ats, and this is recommended (mustahabb), not wajib. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the reasoning behind the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default ruling
The act is reciting a Surah after Fatiha in the first two rak'ats of 'Isha. If missed, what happens? The passage addresses this.
The prayer itself remains valid; only the recitation sequence is affected.
2
List the four intra-Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say: recite only the Surah (not Fatiha) in the last two. Abu Yusuf says: recite neither. A narration from Abu Hanifa says: recite both. 'Isa ibn Aban says: recite only the Fatiha.
The dispute is about whether qada' is possible and which part is made up.
3
Analyze the proof for the majority view
The reasoning: the Fatiha must precede the Surah; making it up in the last two would reverse the order. The Surah, however, can be made up without breaking sequence because it is not tied to a specific position after Fatiha in later rak'ats? Actually, the Surah is normally after Fatiha, but in qada' it can be placed after Fatiha in the last two because the Fatiha is already recited in its proper place? The text says the Surah can be made up in the prescribed manner, while the Fatiha cannot.
This is a talil (reasoning) for the distinction.
4
Determine the preferred position (mufta bihi)
The wording in al-Jami' al-Saghir ('he recites') suggests obligation, but Imam Muhammad in al-Asl uses 'I prefer', indicating recommendation. The later Hanafi masters prefer the latter as the relied-upon view.
Al-Asl is earlier but more explicit; al-Jami' al-Saghir is later but ambiguous. The tarjih weighs clarity over chronological order.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
If you miss the Surah in the first two rak'ats, you may recite it in the last two rak'ats after the Fatiha, and this is recommended (mustahabb). You are not obliged to do so; the prayer is valid either way.
If you choose not to recite it, no compensation (sajdah sahwi) is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو ترك السورة في أولي العشاء قرأها في الاخريين مع الفاتحة جهراً ولو ترك الفاتحة لا يقرؤها في الأخريين وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد. وقال أبو يوسف: لا يقضي واحدة منهما لأن الواجب إذا فات عن وقته لا يقضي إلا بدليل. ولهما الفرق بين الوجهين أن قراءة الفاتحة شرعت على وجه يترتب عليها السورة فلو قضاها في الأخريين تترتب الفاتحة على السورة إذ التقدير أنه قرأ السورة ثم يقضي الفاتحة فتترتب الفاتحة على السورة، وهذا خلاف الموضوع بخلاف ما إذا ترك السورة لأنه أمكن قضاؤها على الوجه المشروع. وهذه المسألة مربعة فالقول الثالث ما رواه الحسن عن أبي حنيفة أنه يقضيهما. وقال عيسى بن أبان: يقضي الفاتحة دون السورة لأنها أهم الأمرين. وفي تعبيره بالخبر في قوله "قرأها" تبعاً للجامع الصغير إشارة إلى الوجوب لأن الإخبار في الوجوب من الأمر. وصرح في الأصل بالاستحباب فإنه قال: أحب إلى أن يقضي السورة في الأخريين. وإنما كان مستحباً لأنه لا يمكن مراعاتها من كل وجه في القضاء لأنها وإن كانت مؤخرة عن الفاتحة فهي غير موصولة بها لأن السورة في الشفع الثاني والفاتحة في الأول. وفي غاية البيان والأصح ما قاله في الجامع الصغير لأنه آخر التصنيفين. وفي فتح القدير: ولا يخفى أن ما في الأصل أصرح فيجب التعويل عليه في الرواية اهـ. وقد يقال أيضاً: إن الإخبار إنما يكون آكد من الأمر أن لو كان من الشارع، أما من الفقهاء فلا يدل على الوجوب بل والأمر منهم لا يدل عليه فكان المذهب الاستحباب ثم ظاهر الكتاب أنه يجهر بالسورة والفاتحة وجعله الشارح ظاهر الرواية وصححه في الهداية لأن الجمع بين الجهر والمخافتة في ركعة شنيع وتغيير النفل وهو الفاتحة أولى وصحح التمرتاشي أنه يجهر بالسورة فقط وجعله شيخ الإسلام الظاهر من الجواب، وفخر الإسلام الصواب قولاً بعدم التغيير. ولا يلزم الجمع بينهما في ركعة لأن السورة تلتحق بموضعها تقديراً ولم يبين كيف يرتبهما، فقيل يقدم السورة وقيل الفاتحة وينبغي ترجيحه وفي قوله "مع الفاتحة" إشارة إلى أنه إذا أراد قضاء السورة ليس له ترك الفاتحة فتصير واجبة كالسورة وفيه قولان، وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب كما هو الأصل فيها. وقيد بكونه ترك الفاتحة في الأوليين لأنه لو نسي من الركعة الأولى أو الثانية وقرأ السورة ثم تذكر قبل الركوع فإنه يأتي بها ويعيد السورة في ظاهر المذهب لأنه إذا أتى بها تكون فرضاً كالسورة فصار كما لو تذكر السورة في الركوع فإنه يأتي بها ويعيد الركوع. (نقله كلام معه ولم يوجد اهـ). ثم الكلام في حقيقة الجهر: قال الكرخي: المراد به الإسماع بحيث يسمع من بقربه، وقال الهندواني: لا بد أن يكون بحيث يسمع نفسه. وقيل: لا بد أن يكون أذناه مسموعاً له. ونقل في المجتبى عن الهندواني أنه لا يجزئه ما لم يسمع اهـ. وفي الذخيرة عن الحلواني أن الأصح هذا، ولا ينبغي أن يجعل قولاً رابعاً بل هو قول الهندواني الأول. وفي العادة إن ما كان مسموعاً له يكون مسموعاً لمن هو بقربه أيضاً. وفي الذخيرة معزياً إلى القاضي علاء الدين أن الأصح عندي أن في بعض التصرفات يكتفي بسماعه وفي بعض التصرفات يشترط سماع غيره مثلاً في البيع لو أدنى المشتري صماخه إلى فم البائع وسمع يكفي ولو سمع البائع بنفسه ولم يسمعه المشتري لا يكفي. وفيما إذا حلف لا يكلم فلاناً فناداه من بعيد بحيث لا يسمع لا يحنث في يمينه. نص على هذا في كتاب الإيمان لأن شرط الحنث وجود الكلام. ثم رأيت العلامة خير الدين الرملي بحث في فتاواه بنحو ما قلته. والحاصل أن في المسألة قولان: قول للكرخي وقول للهندواني والاعتماد على قول الهندواني والله تعالى أعلم.
And if he abandons the Surah in the first two [rak'ats] of 'Isha, he recites it in the last two with the Fatiha aloud, and if he abandons the Fatiha, he does not recite it in the last two according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not make up either of them because when an obligation passes its time, it is not made up except by evidence. Their proof is the difference between the two cases: the recitation of the Fatiha was legislated in a way that the Surah follows it, so if he makes it up in the last two, the Fatiha would come after the Surah, contrary to the prescribed order. But if he abandons the Surah, it can be made up in the prescribed manner. This issue has four positions: the third is what al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he makes up both. 'Isa ibn Aban said: He makes up the Fatiha but not the Surah because it is the more important. In his wording with 'he recited' following al-Jami' al-Saghir, it indicates obligation because in obligation, informing is like commanding. But in al-Asl he stated recommendation, saying: I prefer that he make up the Surah in the last two. It is only recommended because it cannot be observed in every respect in the make-up, since although it is delayed after the Fatiha, it is not connected because the Surah is in the second pair and the Fatiha in the first. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the most correct is what is said in al-Jami' al-Saghir because it is the later of the two works. In Fath al-Qadir: It is not hidden that what is in al-Asl is more explicit, so one must rely on it in narration. It could also be said: Informing is only stronger than commanding if it were from the Lawgiver; from jurists it does not indicate obligation, rather even their command does not indicate it, so the school is recommendation. Then the apparent meaning of the text is that he recites aloud the Surah and the Fatiha, and the commentator made it the apparent position and corrected it in al-Hidayah because combining loud and quiet recitation in one rak'ah is odious, and changing the supererogatory (i.e., the Fatiha) is more appropriate. Al-Tumurtashi corrected that he recites only the Surah aloud, and Shaykh al-Islam made the apparent from the answer, and Fakhr al-Islam [said] the correct position is non-change. There is no need for combining both in one rak'ah because the Surah attaches to its place virtually. And he did not explain how to order them; it is said he recites the Surah first, or the Fatiha first, and the latter should be preferred. In his saying "with the Fatiha" is an indication that if he wants to make up the Surah, he is not allowed to abandon the Fatiha, so it becomes obligatory like the Surah; there are two opinions on this, and preference should be given to non-obligation as is the original principle. He restricted it to abandoning the Fatiha in the first two because if he forgets it in the first or second rak'ah and recites the Surah, then remembers before bowing, he performs it and repeats the Surah in the apparent school because when he performs it, it becomes a fard like the Surah, similar to if he remembers the Surah during bowing, he performs it and repeats the bowing. Then the discussion of the reality of jahr: al-Karkhi said: Its meaning is making [others] hear such that those near him hear. Al-Hindwani said: It is necessary that he hear himself. It was said: It is necessary that his ears hear him. In al-Mujtaba it is narrated from al-Hindwani that it is not sufficient unless he hears. In al-Dhakhira from al-Halwani that this is the most correct. The conclusion is that there are two opinions: the opinion of al-Karkhi and the opinion of al-Hindwani, and reliance is on the opinion of al-Hindwani, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq provides detailed commentary on the ruling for missed recitations in 'Isha prayer. It begins by stating the ruling: if one abandons the Surah in the first two rak'ats, he recites it in the last two along with the Fatiha aloud; but if he abandons the Fatiha, he does not recite it in the last two. This is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Yusuf disagrees, holding that neither is made up because the time for obligatory recitation has passed. The commentators (the two shaykhs) provide the reasoning: the Fatiha is legislated to precede the Surah, so making it up in the last two would reverse the order, while the Surah can be made up without disrupting the sequence. The text then notes that the issue has four positions: another from Abu Hanifa through Hasan ibn Ziyad (makes up both), and from 'Isa ibn Aban (makes up only Fatiha). The author then discusses whether the word 'recites' indicates obligation or recommendation. Although al-Jami' al-Saghir uses the form of informing, which typically indicates obligation, Imam Muhammad in al-Asl uses the word 'I prefer', showing recommendation. The later preference in the school is recommendation (istihbab). Regarding jahr (audible recitation), there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Al-Karkhi defines jahr as making others hear, while al-Hindwani defines it as making oneself hear. The relied-upon position is al-Hindwani's, as confirmed by al-Halwani and al-Ramli. The practical difference emerges in cases like deaf imams or noisy environments. The author concludes that the correct position is that jahr requires the person to hear himself.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed obligatory or recommended act in prayer after its proper time.
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah.
السورة (al-surah): A chapter of the Quran; in prayer, it refers to a Surah recited after the Fatiha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on making up a missed Surah in the last two rak'ats of 'Isha prayer?
A) It is wajib (obligatory).
B) It is mustahabb (recommended).
C) It is haram (forbidden).
D) It is makruh (disliked).

Key Takeaway
Making up a missed Surah in 'Isha prayer is recommended (mustahabb) according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Definition of Jahr in Audible Recitation
Definition of jahr in Hanafi fiqh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define jahr according to the relied-upon Hanafi position and explain the practical consequence of the dispute between al-Karkhi and al-Hindwani.

Core Idea
Jahr means the reciter hears himself; the Hanafi school relies on this definition, not on others hearing.

When the Hanafi school requires audible recitation (jahr) in certain prayers, what exactly is the minimum? There is a dispute among early Hanafi scholars. This lesson unpacks the two main opinions and explains why the definition of al-Hindwani (hearing oneself) is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The question is: what constitutes fulfilling the requirement of jahr in prayer? Is it that others hear, or that oneself hears?
This is relevant for Fajr, Maghrib, and 'Isha prayers for men.
2
State al-Karkhi's position
Al-Karkhi said: jahr means making others hear, i.e., those near the reciter must be able to hear him.
This relies on the literal meaning of 'jahr' (public/audible to others).
3
State al-Hindwani's position
Al-Hindwani said: jahr means the reciter hears himself. It is not necessary that others hear.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.
4
Analyze the tarjih (preference)
The passage cites al-Halwani and al-Ramli in confirming that the correct view is al-Hindwani's. The reasoning includes practicality: in noisy environments or with deaf followers, requiring others to hear would be difficult.
The definition of hearing oneself also aligns with the customary understanding of speaking aloud.
5
Apply in practice
If an imam recites loud enough that he himself can hear, even if those behind him cannot (e.g., due to distance or noise), the requirement of jahr is fulfilled.
The same applies to mukhafatah (silent recitation): one must hear himself, but softly.

Source Text

إلا بدليل. ولهما الفرق بين الوجهين أن قراءة الفاتحة شرعت على وجه يترتب عليها السورة فلو قضاها في الأخريين تترتب الفاتحة على السورة إذ التقدير أنه قرأ السورة ثم يقضي الفاتحة فتترتب الفاتحة على السورة، يرتبهما، فقيل يقدم السورة وقيل الفاتحة وينبغي ترجيحه وفي قوله "مع الفاتحة" إشارة إلى أنه إذا أراد قضاء السورة ليس له ترك الفاتحة فتصير واجبة كالسورة وفيه قولان، وينبغي ترجيح عدم الوجوب كما هو الأصل The Hanafi Internal Dispute on the Minimum Obligatory Recitation in Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fard recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi narrations (riwayat) regarding the minimum fard recitation in prayer, identify the evidence (dalil) for each position, and determine the mufta bihi ruling and its practical application.

Core Idea
The minimum fard recitation is one verse, but its length is disputed: any verse (Abu Hanifa), three short or one long (Sahibayn), or anything called Quran (Quduri).

In this lesson, we delve into the Hanafi internal dispute over the minimum Quranic recitation that fulfills the fard of prayer. While the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states simply 'one verse,' later scholars transmitted three distinct positions from the founding imams. Understanding these positions requires examining both the Quranic evidence and the underlying usul principle regarding the prioritization of linguistic reality versus customary usage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states: 'Wa fard al-qira'ah āyah' — the obligatory recitation is a verse. Determine what 'verse' means linguistically and technically.
The word āyah has multiple definitions; the shortest Quranic verse is 'lam yalid' (5 letters).
2
Distinguish the three narrations
Three positions exist within the Hanafi school: (1) any single full verse (zahir al-riwaya, attributed to Abu Hanifa), (2) whatever is called Quran and not resembling human speech (narration of Quduri), (3) three short verses or one long verse (narration of the Sahibayn). Learn the source for each.
The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is the dominant position in the early school.
3
Examine the proof for each
The primary evidence for the first narration is Quran 73:20 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' — an absolute command without specifying length. The Sahibayn argue that a very short verse does not count as recitation customarily, so the command should be interpreted according to 'urf. The Quduri narration takes a middle ground: anything that is called Quran and is not speech of people.
The dispute also involves the usul principle of al-haqiqa al-musta'mala vs. al-majaz al-mutāraf.
4
Analyze the underlying principle
Abu Hanifa prioritizes the linguistic reality (haqiqa): a short verse is still a verse. The Sahibayn prioritize conventional usage (urf): recitation must be something conventionally recognized as Quranic recitation. Understand how this principle leads to different rulings on specific instances.
The commentator (Ibn Nujaym) discusses the interplay between haqiqa and urf.
5
Apply to specific examples
Test the rulings on specific short Quranic phrases like 'thumma nazara' (11 letters), 'mudhaammatan' (single word), and the isolated letters (huruf muqatta'a) like 'sad', 'qaf', 'nun'. According to Abu Hanifa, these may suffice; according to the Sahibayn, they do not. The Quduri narration allows 'mudhaammatan' but not the letters because they are not called Quran in the same sense.
The commentator notes that later scholars (mashayikh) differed on these examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وفرض القراءة آية) هي في اللغة العلامة الظاهرة ومن هنا سميت المعجزة آية لدلالتها على النبوّة وصدق من ظهرت على يده وتقال الآية لكل جملة دالة على حكم من أحكامه تعالى، ولكل كلام منفصل عما قبله وبعده بفصل توقيفي لفظي، وقيل جماعة حروف وكلمات من قولهم خرج القوم بآيتهم أي بجماعتهم كذا في شرح المصابيح لزين العرب. وفي بعض حواشي الكشاف والآية طائفة من القرآن مترجمة أقلها ستة أحرف صورة اهـ . ويرد عليه قوله تعالى لم يلد ) [الإخلاص : ٣] فإنها آية ولهذا جوز أبو حنيفة الصلاة بها وهي خمسة أحرف. وفي فرض القراءة ثلاث روايات ظاهر الرواية كما نقله المشايخ ما في الكتاب لقوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن [المزمل: ۲۰] من غير فصل إلا أن ما دون الآية خارج منه والآية ليست في معناه وفي رواية ما يطلق عليه اسم القرآن ولم يشبه قصد خطاب أحد وصححه القدوري، ورجحه الشارح بأنه أقرب إلى القواعد الشرعية لأن المطلق ينصرف إلى الأدنى وفيه نظر، بل المطلق ينصرف إلى الكامل في الماهية. وفي رواية ثلاث آيات قصار أو آية طويلة وهو قولهما ورجحه في الأسرار بأنه احتياط لأن قوله ولم يلد [الإخلاص : ٣] ثم نظر ﴾ [المدثر : ۲۱] لا يتعارف قرآناً وهو قرآن حقيقة فمن حيث الحقيقة حرمتا على الحائض والجنب ومن حيث العدم لم تجز الصلاة به حتى يأتي بما يكون قرآناً حقيقة وعرفاً، فالأمر المطلق لا ينصرف إلى ما لا يتعارف قرآناً والاحتياط أمر حسن في العبادات. وذكر المصنف في الكافي أن الخلاف مبني على أصل وهو أن الحقيقة المستعملة أولى عنده من المجاز المتعارف وعندهما بالعكس أطلق الآية فشمل الطويلة والقصيرة والكلمة. ذلك. قوله : (وهي خمسة أحرف أي خمسة صورة ولفظاً وإلا فهي ستة لأن أصل يلد يولد قال في النهر : ثم قيل إن أي الإخلاص أربع ، د وقيل خمس فيجوز أن يكون ما في الحواشي بناء على الأول. قوله: (وفيه نظر (الخ قد يجاب بأن المراد المطلق في باب الأمر والنهي ينصرف إلى الأدنى بمعنى أن العبد يخرج عن عهدة التكليف به لأنه المتحقق وأما الأعلى الكامل فيحتاج إلى دليل خاص، ولذا اكتفى في الأمر بالسجود والركوع عما يتحقق أصلهما دون توقف على الكامل منهما إلا كانت الطمأنينة فرضاً لا واجبة تأمل. وما سيأتي أنه من لو قرأ آية طويلة في ركعتين يجوز عند عامة المشايخ وصححه في المنية، يفيد أرجحية رواية القدوري وتعليل الزيلعي لها وجوابنا عن النظر المذكور. قوله : (وهو أن الحقيقة المستعملة أولى (الخ معناه أن كونه غير قارىء مجاز متعارف وكونه قارئاً بذلك حقيقة مستعملة فإنه لو قيل هذا قارئ لم يخطئ المتكلم نظراً إلى الحقيقة اللغوية. في الفتح وفيه نظر فإنه منع ما دون الآية بناء على عدم كونه قارئاً عرفاً وأجاز الآية القصيرة لأنها ليست في معناه أي في أنه لا يعد به قارئاً بل يعد بها قارئاً عرفاً، فالحق أنه يبتني على الخلاف في قيام العرف في عده قارئاً بالقصيرة قالا : لا يعد وهو يمنع . نعم ذلك مبناه على رواية ما يتناوله قال الواحدة وما كان مسماه حرفاً فيجوز بقوله تعالى ثم نظر ﴾ [المدثر: ۲۱] مدهامتان [الرحمن : ٦٤] ص، ق، ن. ولا خلاف في الأول، وأما في الثاني والثالث ففيه اختلاف المشايخ والأصح أنه لا يجوز لأنه يسمى عاداً لا قارئاً كذا ذكره الشارحون وهو مسلم في ص ونحوه لأن نحو ص ليس بآية لعدم انطباق تعريفها عليه وأما في نحو «مدهامتان» فذكر الاسبيجابي وصاحب البدائع أنه يجوز على قول أبي حنيفة من غير ذكر خلاف بين المشايخ، وما وقع في عبارة المشايخ من أن ص ونحوه حرف فقال في فتح القدير: إنه غلط فإنها كلمة مسماها حرف وليس المقروء وإنما المقروء صاد وقاف ونون
The statement: (And the fard of recitation is a verse) – In language, it is a manifest sign, hence the miracle is called aya because it indicates prophethood and truthfulness of the one through whom it appears. An aya is also said of every complete sentence indicating a ruling of Allah, and of every distinct speech separated from what precedes and follows by a fixed verbal separation. It is also said to be a group of letters and words, from the saying 'the people went out with their aya (i.e., their group)'. As in Sharh al-Masabih by Zain al-Arab. In some glosses on al-Kashshaf: 'An aya is a group of the Qur'an consisting of at least six letters in form.' End. It is objected by His saying 'lam yalid' (Surah al-Ikhlas: 3) because it is an aya, yet Abu Hanifa permitted prayer with it, and it is five letters. Regarding the fard of recitation, there are three narrations: The apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) as transmitted by the mashayikh is what is in the book (i.e., the matn) because of His saying 'faqra'u ma tayassara min al-Qur'an' (al-Muzzammil: 20) without specification, except that less than a verse is excluded, and a verse is not in its meaning. In another narration: whatever is called the name of the Qur'an and does not resemble the intent of addressing someone, and al-Quduri authenticated it, and the commentator preferred it because it is closer to the legal principles since the absolute is directed to the minimum, but there is a consideration: rather the absolute is directed to the complete in essence. In another narration: three short verses or one long verse – this is their (the Sahibayn's) view, and it was preferred in al-Asrar because it is precautionary, because His statement 'lam yalid' and 'thumma nazara' (al-Muddaththir: 21) is not conventionally known as Qur'an although it is genuinely Qur'an. So from the perspective of reality, it is restricted for a menstruating woman and a junub, and from the perspective of absence, prayer with it is not valid until one brings what is genuinely and conventionally Qur'an. The absolute command is not directed to what is not conventionally known as Qur'an, and precaution is good in worship. The author mentioned in al-Kafi that the difference is based on a principle: that the used reality is prioritized over the conventional metaphor according to him (Abu Hanifa), while with them (the Sahibayn) it is the opposite. He (the matn) used the word 'aya' absolutely, so it includes long and short and a word. That is it. The statement: (And it is five letters) means five in form and word, otherwise it is six because the root of yalid is yulidu. The author said in al-Nahr: 'Then it is said that Ikhlas has four, and it is said five, so what is in the glosses may be based on the first.' The statement: 'And there is a consideration' may be answered that the absolute in matters of command and prohibition is directed to the minimum in the sense that the servant fulfills the obligation because it is realized, while the higher complete requires specific evidence, hence in the command of sajda and ruku', what suffices for their realization is enough without the complete, unless tranquility is fard not wajib. Consider. And what will come that if one reads a long verse in two rak'ats, it is permissible according to general mashayikh and authenticated in al-Munya, indicates the precedence of Quduri's narration and al-Zayla'i's reasoning and our response to the mentioned consideration. The statement: (And that is that the used reality is prioritized) means that his being not a reader is a conventional metaphor, and his being a reader with that is a used reality, for if one says 'this is a reader', the speaker would not be wrong considering linguistic reality. In al-Fath: 'And there is a consideration', because he prevented less than a verse based on the fact of not being a reader conventionally, and allowed a short verse because it is not in its meaning, i.e., he is not considered a reader with it but is considered a reader with it conventionally. So the truth is that it depends on the dispute concerning the determination of custom in counting him a reader with a short verse: they (the Sahibayn) say he is not counted, and he (Abu Hanifa) prevents. Yes, that is based on the narration of what it includes. He said: One (word) and what is called a letter is permissible with His saying 'thumma nazara' (al-Muddaththir: 21), 'mudhaammatan' (al-Rahman: 64), 'sad', 'qaf', 'nun'. There is no dispute regarding the first. As for the second and third, there is difference among the mashayikh, and the most correct is that it is not permissible because it is called a counter, not a reader, as the commentators mentioned, and this is accepted regarding 'sad' and the like because 'sad' is not an aya due to the inapplicability of its definition, but regarding 'mudhaammatan', al-Isbijabi and the author of al-Bada'i narrated that it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa without any dispute among the mashayikh. And what occurred in the expressions of the mashayikh that 'sad' and the like are letters, then it is said in Fath al-Qadir: it is a mistake, for it is a word whose name is a letter, and it is not what is recited; rather what is recited is 'sad', 'qaf', and 'nun'.
Source pages p. 591

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the obligatory minimum recitation in prayer. It begins by defining the term 'aya' both linguistically and technically, then proceeds to the three narrations within the Hanafi school regarding what constitutes the fard of recitation. The author discusses the proofs for each position: Abu Hanifa holds that any single verse, even a short one like 'lam yalid' (5 letters), is sufficient based on the absolute command in Surah al-Muzzammil. The Sahibayn require a verse that is conventionally recognized as such, i.e., three short verses or one long verse, which they support via precaution (ihtiyat). A third narration attributed to Quduri requires whatever is called 'Qur'an' without resembling ordinary speech. The commentary then examines the underlying legal principle (al-asl) that the used reality (al-haqiqa al-musta'mala) is prioritized over conventional metaphor according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn give priority to conventional usage. The passage concludes with specific rulings on whether certain short phrases from the Qur'an (like 'thumma nazara', 'mudhaammatan', and the single letters 'sad', 'qaf', 'nun') can fulfill the fard, noting the differences among later scholars and affirming the correct position.

Key Terms
آية (āyah): A verse of the Qur'an; in this context, any complete sentence or phrase separated by a fixed verbal division. The minimum number of letters is disputed (5 or 6).
فرض القراءة (farḍ al-qirā'ah): The obligatory minimum recitation of Qur'an during the prayer; the amount required to make the prayer valid.
الرواية (al-riwāyah): A transmitted narration or version of a legal ruling within the Hanafi school, particularly from the founding imams.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) in the Hanafi school, what is the obligatory minimum recitation in prayer?
A) One full verse of any length.
B) Three short verses or one long verse.
C) Surah al-Fatiha only.
D) Any phrase that is called Qur'an.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes three valid narrations on the minimum fard recitation, with the zahir al-riwaya being one verse, but the mufta bihi remains open to ihtiyat (precaution) in practice.
